O, sons, because I have completed this book for you, which is the last of the science of medicine, by its fulfillment its end is achieved in it, and by its expositions, and by its declarations, it is my view that you complete this to you with this treatise, which is a part of the operation with me, so it is my surgery.
Because the operation with me is prostrate in our region and in our time entirely deprived, whereas it is greatly perilous the science of it, and its vestiges are held hostage; and there remains of it only some small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which have been altered and have become subject to those errors and uncertainties, because their clauses are understood and the strength of it and the art are elongated.
And it is seen to me that you bring to life that with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and because it comes with the forms of the tools of cautery and the other instruments of the work as it is by addition of the declaration, and by preparation of it, which cause is necessary.
But the cause for which no one has been found to be a good artificer with his hand in this our time, is that the art of medicine is long, and that it requires the actor to be exercised before it in the science of anatomy, which reconciles Gualia in that he knows the movements of the members and the forms of those, and the conjunction and separation of them; and to have the knowledge of the bones, the nerves and the cartilages, and the number of those, and the egress of them; and of the pulsatile veins and the quiet ones, and the places of the effusion of those.
And for that reason, it is said by Hippocrates that in name it is small, but in the work it is great, and most of all in the art of the hand.
But now we have already said of that in the introduction of this book; for whoever is not learned in what we have said of anatomy, it is not evacuated that he does not fall into error for which many men die, as I have seen too many of those, for some are formed in this science and cast themselves away from that knowledge and their experience.
For I saw a foolish and inept physician who had incised an abscess scrophilos in the neck of a woman, and incised some arteries of the neck so that much blood flowed, and the woman died among her hands.
And I saw another physician who prescribed that the throat of a man who had been in his state be purged, and the stone was large, and it came to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, so that that man on the third day died.
And I had already been called to extract that, and I saw that because of the greatness of the stone and the disposition of the patient, I recognized over him that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was taking a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he was given a black castrated man who was broken in the hip; and prepared the physician with his ignorance, I extracted the fracture, over the wound, with splints and splints with strong structure, and I did not leave the wound to breathe.
And then he set it according to his desires, and he bound it, and then he left it for some days and commanded that we untie the bandage; and it came to be so that the hip and the foot were festered, and it came to ruin.
And I was called to him, and I helped to untie the bandage, and obtained tranquility and then eased his pains.
But however, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, so that I could not stop it, and it did not cease to wander the corruption in the limb until the patient perished.
And I saw another physician who perforated a cancerous abscess, and it was ulcerated after some days, until the evil of it was magnified to its lord.
The cause of which is that the cautery is pure of melancholic humor, therefore it does not come to it with iron of all, but that it be in a member which suffers that it be all held hostage.
And therefore, sons, it is necessary to you that the operation with me be devised in two divisions: so it is in operation to which is associated health, and in work with which is peril in the major dispositions.
And I have already stated this in all places of this book in which I bring operation in which is error and fear; for it is necessary to you that you guard this and leave that, so that the fools do not find a way to speak and to dishonor you.
And therefore, take your arms with diligence and with the protection of God, and your patients with facility and with firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God, pursuing health and laudable success, and leave the diseases terrible of difficult healing, and hold your arms from that which makes you fear, so that hesitation in your faith and in your name does not escape you: for more is remaining to your glory, and more in the world and in the end to your sanctities.
Gualia already said in some of his admonitions: “Do not treat a bad disease, so that bad physicians you are not called.”
And now I have divided this book according to three chapters.
Begins the division of the book, and first of the first part. The first chapter ordered of the head within feet, in the forms of the instruments and in the tools of the cauteries, and of that which is necessary in the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, of suction and perforation, and of leeches, and of poultices, and of the extraction of arrows and of things similar to them, all chaptered and ordered by the forms of the instruments.
The third chapter, of restoration and dislocation, and of the cure of twisting and of things similar to them; chapter ordered of the head within feet, and of the forms of the instruments.
Know that you should say the quality of the judgments of that cautery and of its inconveniences, and in what completion it should be prohibited cautery.
Therefore I say that the sermon of the quality of the judgment of cautery and of its inconveniences is a long and prolix sermon, and subtle by science, and secretly hidden; and already of it have spoken a great multitude of wise men, and of it they have been disagreed, and to me suffices a little of the sermons of theirs, fearing prolongation.
And therefore I say that cautery compares to all complections universally which are in matter or have matter, except for two complections, which are complections which have no matter.
In the dry and thin complection with matter they disagreed; for some said that cautery is beneficial to that, and the others said the contrary of that, that cautery is not convenient in illness which is by quality and by dryness, because the nature of fire is quality and dryness, and inconvenient is that illness dry and thin with that which is hot and dry be healed.
And they say those who say the contrary of that, that by cautery is made benefit in all dry and thin illness that comes in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and its humidities to the complexion of fire, you find the body of man cold.
And I say for the sermon of that, that experience this already to me some times has discovered.
May, however, it not come upon this that which already is exhausted and exercised in the chapter of cautery by prior exercise, and who has known the diversity of the complexion of men and the disposition of the illnesses in their own bodies, and the causes of those, and their accidents, and the space of time of those.
May in the other complections, there is no fear upon you, and more especially in the cold and humid illnesses, because already all the physicians have agreed upon those, and do not disagree in the judgment with cautery in those.
And know, sons, that of the secret of cure by cautery with fire and of its goodness, is because the fire is simple, the action of which does not reach beyond the member which is cauterized and does not touch the other member attached to it except with a little inconvenience.
But the action of burning medicine reaches that in the members which are distant from it, and greatly makes them come in the member illness of difficult healing and greatly increases.
But fire, by its sublimity and of its substance goodness, does not do this except that it is superfluous. And already it is to us known by experiment and by length of service of study in the truth of the causes; and for that I am excused of the length of the sermon, and if it were not that it is not read in my book in this pause to you secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in the bodies and of its expulsion by which it expels the illnesses, with philosophical and demonstrative sermon, which would be acute in your minds.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to do cautery and pause the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because so that the inconvenience for the accidental time is submerged in the benefit of that which with the cautery is aimed, and more especially if the cautery is for pains or of necessary pains, strong and fistulous, which do not suffer delay because it is feared of those that come malice, which is greater than a little inconvenience entering for time.
And so do not catch in your minds, or, sons, that this is not esteemed by the vulgar people and the foolish physicians, because it is that to that illness which is healed by cautery is not reduced at all times, and they pause that consequence.
And the cause is not at all so as they care for that, because cautery is nothing but in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humidities which are the cause for which the pains come.
But however, cautery is superfluous over medicine by the will of its value and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that its illness returns at any hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of its illness, and the virtue of it, and what is prepared in the body of it of the aggregation of the superfluities in it, and what has reached it in its acquisition in foods and things similar to those causes; unless that the illness in which cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member of few superfluities and humidities, as cautery of tooth for pain and things similar to that, it is possible that in it it does not return that pain, but rather that it is done in smalls.
And more commonly spoken is that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, and it is rightly spoken, for I do not understand what is said about it, because I believe that there is no cure that would benefit with medicine or with any other cause more than cauterization.
And the cause is contrary to that; and the understanding that cauterization is the last remedy of medicine is only when they administer the methods of cure in some diseases, and those medicines do not confer, and then at the end of the cause one administers cauterization, and it benefits to that. And therefore, because cauterization is the last remedy of medicine, not according to the understanding which I understand the common people and many of the foolish physicians.
And the ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than cauterization with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cauterization does not make a scar, as it is not absolutely true, because I have already seen that and I have found that it does not do that except in some bodies, and cauterization with that is good and better than with iron as they said; however, when you make cauterization with fire of gold, it is not declared to you, because it is ignited according to the quantity that you want for the heat of the gold, and because it prepares to receive heat; and if you adjust it over the fire, the gold melts by the fire, and in the fire some plates so that the craftsman catches for the occupation of that.
And for that reason cauterization with iron must be done more lightly and more properly to the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on cauterization according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head among the feet, so that later the one who asks for it may have what he wants from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization confers on the humidity and coldness over the nerve affected by the two causes of which it is the cause of soda and multitude of rheumatic flux, called corissa, from the head to the parts of the ears and the ears flow, and multitude of sleep, and pain of teeth and of the throat, and universally of all illness that comes from coldness, as well as paralytically, soda and apoplexy, and similar in those illnesses.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first you command the patient to be evacuated with laxative medicine the head modifying, for three or for four nights, according to what requires the virtue of the patient and the age of him and his custom.
And then command him to shave his head, and then make that seizure between your hands on a low bench and that he place his hands on his feet.
And then place the root of your palm near the nose between his heels. But however, as the tip of your finger has arrived at the place, sign that place with a tent, and then ignite the cauterizing olive of which this is the form:
And then place that upon the place marked with a tent, in the manner that it descends, with which your hand be constricted little by little, and you revolve that.
And then lift your hand slightly and look at the place, and if you see already of the bone being uncovered any quantity of the head, as well as the quantity of a grain of peas, then raise your hand, and if not return your hand with that iron, with another of that, if it is cooled, until it is seen of the bone what I have told you.
And then take a little salt and dissolve that over the place and leave that for three days.
And then place on it a poultice embedded in a border and leave that on it until the scar of the fire is destroyed. And then cure the place with tetrapharmacon ointment until it is healed.
And already they said that when the plague remains open, so much better gets the scar, because it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the bone should be cauterized into the bone, and that the cauterizer should be held until some part of the surface of the bone is burned.
And then be scraped that which is burned of the bone, and then be cured.
And others said that with the cauterizer it should reach the end, until it presses into the bone forcefully until the bone breaks, and this is the form of alphecati small: And they estimate that from that place the vapors of the head expire.
And let the plague be kept open for a long time, and then be cured until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two kinds of cauterization have not been seen at all, except in some men according to their way of fear; and leaving that, I, in my opinion, is better for health, when it is; because the head is revealed by the solution of continuity of it as we have testified in the other members, and more so when the head of the patient is of a cold nature.
And the kind of cauterization first is more saved and better, in my opinion; and from that, I and with that work with health.
Second Chapter.
Of the cauterization of the head.
When chronic and long-lasting pain occurs throughout the head, and it is prolonged in the patient, and they use herbs and potions and purgatives and plasters and poultices and ointments and compresses and remedies, and mostly if it has already been cauterized with a cautery which is recounted and does not benefit them from any of those causes, then consider that if the head of the patient is of strong creation in its nature; and it is not frail and finds a very great burn, then cauterize it with another cautery besides that one a little. Then cauterize that one on the horn of their head with a cautery until the bone is parted. Incise the bone and discover the quantity which we have recounted and cauterize that one with a cautery in the rear part of the head in the place which is called the basin—and that is the place in which a cupping glass is placed. And alleviate your hand in this, and do not discover the bone, for the patient by this finds a very great pain different from the pain of all the other cauterizations of the head.
And you say this cautery in its place, because the cautery with which you cauterize the horns of the head and the nape is more subtle cautery than that with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Chapter Third.
Of cauterization of old non-antique.
When pain in the head is felt, or pain is spread into the eye, it is evacuated with medicines that modify the head, and the other cure is administered, which I have said in the divisions of the diseases; and if none of them benefits, then cauterization in it is in two ways: either cauterization with a sharp, burning medicine, or with iron.
But cauterization with burning medicine is that you take a piece of alum, and you choose that one and cut off the extremities of it from both ends. And then incise the place of the pain in the temple with a lancet laid until there is a place made in it behind the bone, until it is hidden.
And then strengthen over it with a stopper by descending constriction, and leave it for the space of three hours; and then untie it and take off the alum, and leave the wound for two or three days, and then place over it a poultice submerged in broth until the place forms a crust.
And then cure that with an enema until it is healed.
And if you wish, do this with some burning medicines which I have written in the two treatises of burning medicines.
But cauterization with iron according to this manner: ignite a cautery of which this is the form:
and it is called a clove cautery, because the head of it is as shaped as a clove in which there is some curvature, and in the middle part of it is a small eminence.
And then place it over the place of the pain, and hold your hand—so that the artery which is behind is not burned—and revolve the iron little by little with speed.
And if the quantity of it that is burned by the thickness of the bone is as much as the majority of it, and elevate your hand so that the artery which is behind is not burned, so that there comes no flow of blood.
And then immerse a poultice in salt water and place that over the place, and leave it for three days; and then place a poultice crushed with broth, and then cure with an enema until it is healed.
And if you wish, cauterize with the extremity of the scalpel according to cautery, and guard yourself from incision of the artery in this proper non-antique migraine.
Chapter Fourth.
Of cauterization of old migraine.
When you cure migraine with what we have said of the previous cure, and what we have said in the divisions of the diseases, and it does not benefit the cure, and sometimes because of the illness that does not reach it what we have said of the first cauterization with medicine or the cauterization with fire, then you cover the scalpel cautery until it is white-hot, because it signifies over the place of the pain with a line of length of which is the majority of it, or which one of those; and pause your hand for a moment and strengthen it until you incise the artery and it reaches into the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to guard against the continuation of the mandible, which is bad for chewing, and that the ligament is not burned and the nerve which harms that, and that it does not become a spasm.
And if it is about the custody and caution of the flow of blood from the artery that is incised, because in the incision of it there is fear, and mostly to that one who ignores what is done and is not studious and experienced; and leaves the operation to him at the beginning.
And you will come with remembrance of the regimen of blood flow accident of the artery according to its manner, in its place in this book.
And if you see of this illness that does not reach this cautery and you see the body of the patient tolerable, cauterize that in the middle part of the head as we have recounted, and cure the wound until it is healed.
And if you will, administer the cautery which we have mentioned in the chapter of the streccio of arceria, with a cautery having two handles, and this cauterization is better and more convenient.
Chapter V.
Of cauterization of the pains of the ears.
When in the ear there is pain due to heat and it is cured with laxative causes and with the other cure which I have said in the division, and the pain is not removed, then ignite the cautery, and this is the one which has the name "puncta", of which this is the form:
And with the "puncta" ignited, and it is moved around the entire ear as a wheel is rotated, or in the circuit of whichever part if the pain is in whichever. Lengthen it with the cautery from the root of the ear little by little as much as you feel the location with the touch.
And if the cautery of ten points in the whole ear, and that one, and then cure the places while they are healing.
Chapter VI.
Of cauterization of tumors.
A tumor which is cured and by cauterization is only of the kinds which come from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of the illnesses.
Avoid cauterization of the kind that comes from dryness or spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that kind of tumor with poultices and capipurgi and gargles, and if you do not find comfort in your cure, then you must cauterize the tumor with three cauteries: the first you must at the root of the ear, the second a little from its temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips.
And pause your cautery for the opposite side of the diseased part, because softening does not come except in the part that is healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize that with the cautery in the right of the extremity of the ear more sovereign a little above the horn of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which be according to the length of the finger, and pause your hand with the cautery until the quantity of the majority of the species of the cordena is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is special of the cutler, the form of which is shown. But however more subtle is that one a little so as you see; and that handle in its place of superfluous thickness a little.
And then cure the place with that which is shown before until it is healed.
Chapter VII.
Of cauterization of old apoplexy.
When apoplexy is old and you cure that with the water which we have said and you do not find comfort in your medication and the disease has no fever, then cauterize that with four cauteries: on top of all the horns of its head; and with the cautery and the middle part of the head, as we have said; and with the cautery in the cheekbone. And the manner of the cautery is made according to what has been said before.
And it is already cauterized above the mouth of the stomach; and it is more behind; and then it is cured with the water which proceeds.
Chapter VIII.
Of cauterization of forgetfulness made by flame.
Then give to the patient at the beginning large poultices and pills of the  servel modifying.
And then shave the head of the patient and place on the cheekbone of him a plaster of cente described in the treatise of plasters.
And pause that several times, for that is the manner of cauterization. And do that according to that same order which I have already said.
And therefore if by those he is healed well; and if not, then make to him three cauteries in the rear part of his head, which are descending from the most sovereign part of the head into the part more below the neck. And pause between each cautery the thickness of the finger, and then cure the cautery with the water which proceeds.
But if you add to it and the patient is that water tolerant, then make to him cauteries in the middle part; and if you want greater addition, then cauterize that above the two horns.
Then cure that until it is healed; and be the cautery olive according to the form given before.
Chapter IX.
Of cauterization of paralysis and of softening of the whole body.
Then you must process in softening the head with poultices and with the water which we have said; and then shave the head of the patient, and then cauterize that with the cautery in the middle part of the head, and with the cautery on top of all the horns of the head, and with the cautery on the rear part of it, and with three cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck.
And if it is necessary in the disease of softening of the body of too much that and the diseases tolerant and the disease is strong, then cauterize that with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the loins, and certainly with the cautery until it is burned of the cord of it, and raise your hand. And then take care of that one who is being healed, and this one is an olive cautery.
Chapter X.
Of cauterization of epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, but rather that epilepsy is due to phlegm.
And therefore, if you modify the brain of him at the beginning of him with years and with the other cure which we have said in the division when the patient is great and is tolerating the excess of the medicines.
And if it is a child who does not suffer the medicines, then administer guarguargisms and mastigators to the serving brain, before that for a few days, with the blessing of the foods.
And then scrape the head of the patient, and then cauterize him with a cautery in the middle location of the head according to the previous manner, and with another cautery in the occiput of him, and on each horn of his head cauterize. And if the patient is strong and is tolerating, then cauterize him with cauteries the ones which I have said, having paralytically and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And be an olive cautery according to what has been preceded.
But if the patient is a child, then pause cautery subtle according to this manner.
Chapter XI.
Of cauterization of melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are humidities corrupted and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we have said in the having paralysis.
And if the cause of melancholy is superfluity declining to melancholy, and the body of the patient is humid, then give him to drink water that purifies the brain of him according to what has preceded in the division.
And then scrape the head of the patient, and then make a proper torticolis on him over the circle, and then place that in the middle location of the head.
And the patient be sensed  castrated, and be held from every part.
And then pause liniment; and it is more worthy of bordering ointment of sheep. And warm that over the fire for a moderate heating by measure, which the said suffers when it is most in him. And then pour that in the middle location of the head of him in the circle, and let him inside that be cooled.
And make water with the patient every week once, with the other regimen of him well inside that he is healed; or if you want, cauterize this making small points according to the best of him, unless that you have the hand with a cautery so ordered: this is a special cautery which moistens the brain with equality.
And then pause that coated in ointment or in grease of quail.
Chapter XII.
Of cauterization of  water descending in the heel.
When to you is declared the beginning of water in the heel by the signs which I have said in the division, then begin and give to the patient to drink water that purifies the head of him, and guard that from all humidities.
And make that suzar in bath in degu for some days.
And then command him to scrape his head, and cauterize that with a cautery in the middle location of the head; and then cauterize that with two cauteries over two temples if it is the beginning of  ysement of water in two heels, or of one side if it is the beginning of the water in one heel.
Incise with cautery all the veins and arteries which are left the codena; and be the cauteries in that length in the latitude of the temples.
And guard yourself from fluxes of blood when it is cauterized; and if you see of him fluxes of blood, stop him with some medicine, the which is to you possible.
And you will come with wisdom which is in the extraction of arteries and in the abscess of those and caution of fluxes of blood.
And some times it is cauterized in the cervix below two bones with two cauteries deliberately produced.
Chapter XIII.
Of cauterization of old tears.
When tears from the heels are old and by the veins and arteries which are in the manifest location of the head outside and it is verified that that is superfluity frigid phlegmatic, then cauterize that with the cautery which we have recounted in the chapter of the beginning of water  falling in the heels, and with a cautery in the middle location of the head and with two cauteries in the cervix below two temples, and with two cauteries in the cervix below two bones. And if you need of addition, then cauterize that in all the latz of the tail of the heel above the extremity of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Chapter XIV.
Of cauterization of stench of the nose.
When you medicate him with the water which we have said in the division and it does not profit your medication, then you prepare and give to the patient the cochias to drink for three nights; and then scrape the head of him, and cauterize him with a middle cautery with an olive cautery. And then cauterize that with a clove cautery with two cauteries on the two eyebrows leaving the hair a little.
And guard yourself from the artery that you do not burn that.
And of the clove cautery this is the form.
Chapter XV.
Of cautery for softening of eyelids of the eyes.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by illness or by humidity, then cauterize that eyelid with a cautery with this lunar cautery; and this is the form of it:
And if you, cauterize that on the two eyebrows a little with two cauteries in all parts, and they are elongated from the temples. And let the length of each cautery be according to the quantity of the eyebrow.
And do not press too hard your hand with the cautery, but according to the quantity that the third part of the eyelid be cauterized.
Chapter XVI.
Of cautery of the eyelid of the eye when the hairs are converted to the parts of themselves and pierce the eye.
When the hairs of the eye are converted to the parts of themselves so that they pierce the eye, cauterize in those two ways, whether cauterize or it is with a medicine comburent.
If with cautery of it with fire, command the patient in front of that he may see his hairs as those which they are cleaned, until they are prolonged and equal; and if pierce that of you must their nament, then you strengthen the eyes of him with a bandage so that it not be bad until the hairs are born.
Therefore, as they are born and equal, then place the head of the patient in your own, and then send over the eyelid of the eyes of him with tent, with a sign which is according to the figure of a leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs.
And then place a cloth soaked in  oil of  or in a mucilage of ptilli over the eye.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form of it.
And then cauterize over the figure which you have marked, little by little, in many times, until the surface of the skin which is as a myrtle leaf, be all burned properly.
And the sign of health of your work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already be contracted and the hairs of it be elevated above the puncture of the eye.
And therefore elevate your hand and leave that for three days, and then place over it a cloth with border until the scab be eradicated. And then cure that with an enguent until it be healed.
But if returns for the hairs any cause to their nament and the eyelid is softened, then do another time the cautery over that all as you had done first.
But if the hairs are in the eyelid, then cauterize that until it be elevated to its natural place and be equal and that the hairs do not pierce the eye.
But the cautery with medicine comburent this is that you command the patient that he may see the hairs until they are prolonged and equal, and then be made of cloth the shape of a myrtle leaf.
And then take of sabot known and of live cautery one. i.e. or that, and then mix those causes well, and make that with a festinacio so that it not be frozen; and then expand of that over the cloth which is made as the shape of a myrtle leaf, and place that over one eye or both; and place over the eye a cloth soaked in oil of , and the head of the patient be in your own.
And place the said over the medicine and press that a little and not the mauguas until the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for bite is in him as of fire.
And therefore as he will perceive that the other bite, then leave the medicine and mau that with your own said; therefore as ceases the bite, then remove the medicine and wash the eye with water; and then consider if times the eyelid already is elevated as it is washed above the constriction with fire or with incision, for then it is well; and if it does not return over that of the medicine on the place in which it has not put the medicine and does not degrade until it be equal your operation and be contracted the eye.
And then place over it a cloth with border until the scab of the adhesion be eradicated, and then cure that with an enguent deafinicon or with another until it be healed.
And it is necessary to you, above your operation that you guard with pervigil diligence that in the eye does not fall re of the medicine, and if the eyelid about some days is softened and some cause of the hairs pierce in the eye, then iterate your medicine over that place the which of the eyelid is softened, and properly as you had done at the beginning, and then enaviro him until it be healed.
And this is the form of a myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men are diversified according to the magnitude and the smallness, and therefore according to that is made your constriction.
And the path of rectum should not be hidden from him who is studying this art.
Chapter XVII.
Of cauterization of a fistula that is in the lacrimal of the heel.
When you cure a fistula with what we have said in the divisions of the diseases and do not confer your cure, then you must cauterize it in this way: command the patient to place their head on your lap, and hold the head of him some minister between your hands in such a way that it is not disturbed nor agitated with his head.
And then place a cloth soaked in oil or in a poultice of ptilli on the heel of him.
And then ignite the cautery of which this is the form:
Which is concave, as is the shape of a reed or a vulture's feather, from one extremity of which the cautery is made.
And if you want, it should be penetrating into the other extremity. And if you want it to be shaped like a tentacle.
But however, the one that is concave is better for your work.
And then press the fistula if it is open, and draw from it pus and dry it. And if it is not open, then open it and extract the pus from it.
And then place on it the cautery which is well ignited, and hold it with your hand a little from the cautery of the heel to the side of the nose, so that it does not burn your hand or the patient be agitated, and then place the cautery in the grooves of the heel and corrupt it.
And therefore if at the beginning of your cautery it penetrates into the bone, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if it is necessary; and leave it like that for three days, and then place on it a cloth with border and surround it with an exsiccative enema until it is healed.
But if after eleven days it is not healed, then place on it a sharp corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered and scraped according to what you have prescribed in your chapter.
And there is another way of cauterizing a fistula which some first-dayers: understand the place of the fistula and make a cut there and then place in that fissure a fine thread of which is the shape: And melt in that a quantity of one ounce of lead; and hold your hand with a fine retention, and do not disturb the patient so that the molten lead does not reach the heel of him; and when you place on the heel of the patient a cloth soaked in oil or in water, because lead will burn the place of the fistula and heal it by a miraculous healing.
And if the fistula is healed with what we have said of the cautery and the cure, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to administer a traction of the nose and reduce the fistula to the nose of the body according to what will come in its proper place.
Chapter XVIII.
Of cauterization of the fissure of the anus.
Many times fissures occur in the lips, and mostly in the lips of children.
Therefore, as you cure those fissures with what we have said in the divisions and do not profit from your cure, then ignite the small cautery knife according to this form that is taught:
And let its concavity be according to the fineness of a needle.
Then place that ignited cautery carefully in those fissures until the cautery reaches the bottom of the fissures.
And then cure that with cerotz until it is healed.
Chapter XIX.
Of cauterization of a fistula in the mouth.
When in the root of the uvula or in the palate or in the roots of the teeth there develops an abscess and then it breaks, and then it is cured, and pus flows and a fistula is made, and then you cure it and do not profit from the cure, then you must ignite the cautery according to the quantity that is received in the fistula, and then put that ignited one in the tract of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the burning iron reaches the bottom of it, and after it you do this once or twice; and then cure it with the water that we have said of the cure until it is healed.
And therefore if the pus is abscessed and is healed, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and host the corrupted bone according to what will come in its chapter.
Chapter XX.
Of cauterization of the teeth and softening of the gums.
When the gums are softened by humidity and the teeth are bad, and you cure those with medicines and do not confer, then place the head of the patient on your lap, and then ignite the cautery the shape of which will come near so that you place the nozzle on the tooth and introduce into it the ignited cautery quickly, and hold your hand a little so that the patient feels the heat of the fire at the root of the tooth being reached.
And then take your hand, and then repeat the cautery several times according to what you want.
And then the patient rinses his mouth with salt water and keeps it there for an hour, and then spits it out, because the bad tooth is stopped, the gum is softened and strengthened, and the corrupted humidity is dried.
Chapter XXI.
Of cauterizing tooth pain.
When tooth pain is due to cold, or there is a worm in it, or it does not respond to treatment with medicine, then cauterization is done in that tooth in two ways: cauterization with a cow's horn, or cauterization with fire.
Cauterization with horn is that you take the horn of a cow and heat it in a blacksmith's forge, and then take a handle and wrap it over the tip of the iron, and then immerse that in the heated horn, and place it on the painful tooth firmly until it is burned.
And then repeat that several times until the force of the fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, submerge wool or a stick in the heated horn below, and place it on the painful tooth, and place a heated iron over it until the iron reaches the bottom of the cavity of the tooth.
But however, cauterization with fire is that you attend to the nozzle of the iron or of fire, and that in the heart of it there is some thickness and the sharpness of the fire does not reach the mouth of the patient.
And then ignite the cauterizer, the shape of which will come, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand over it until the cauterizer is burned; and do this several times because the pain will be removed either on that day or the next day.
And so that by the impression of that cauterizer the patient rinses his mouth with good broth and keeps it there for an hour and then spits it out; and this is the shape of the cauterizer.
And cauterize with whatever extremity you wish according to what is possible for you.
And this is the shape of the cannula:
Chapter XXII.
Of cauterization of tumors.
When tumors are of phlegm and of cold humors and do not respond to digestion by medicines and you wish the digestion of those slightly, then you ignite the cauterizer whose shape is this following, having two open extremities so that the smoke of the cauterizer escapes from the other extremity, and place it on that abscess once, and another if you judge it necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess.
And if the abscess is small, then place the cauterizer according to the size of the abscess, and then leave it for three days and place a stick soaked in broth over it until that which the fire has burned is removed.
And then cure that with gargles and poultices and bandages until it is healed.

Of cauterization of hoarseness of voice and constriction of the throat.

And cauterize that with another cauterizer at the junction of the neck at the lower vertebra of it. And the cauterizer of it be a pointed one according to the previous manner.
And then cure that with the water that is preceded until it is healed.

And then cauterize the tendon while it penetrates into the other side; and the figure of cauterization will then be of four cauteries.

Chapter .xliii.
Of cauterization at the beginning of inflammation.

And if it does not descend below, you know that it is water.
But if it is not prepared the descent of the sania with water that we have said, then make the patient lie between your hands and then take a fine spatula and fen it on that over the pannicol, carefully severing the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea in the corona (in the place where it is vacant), until the sania is discharged.
Therefore, as it is discharged, then you distill into the wound water cauda in which you have mixed honey or water in which you have already boiled fennel and honey.
And then cure it with the other causes until it is healed.
Chapter XXII.
Of the cure of the descending water from the wound.
We have already said the kinds of water in the division and which ones it is convenient to pierce with a serum, declaring, then this according to the health.
Now, you must make the patient lie between your hands on a board and tie his wound shut, tight.
And then place your left hand near the eyelid of his wound if the wound with the water is the left one; or on your right hand, if the wound is the right one.
And then with your right hand, take an almond, if the wound is left; or with your left hand, if the wound is right.
And then place the extremity of the almond near the corona for the thickness of the ray in the album of the wound from the side of the lacrimal gland, and then peel the almond with virtue and roll your hand on it.
And then penetrate into the album of the wound and feel that the almond has already arrived at the vacant cause.
And it is necessary that the measure of the path of the almond to the bottom is the measure of the space which is from the pupil to the end of the blackness, and it is the corona of the wound; because you will see with that pupil the vision of the wound through the clarity of the tunic cornea.
And then place the almond into the place where the water is, and then you throw it down once, then another, and then if the water descends quickly, then you wet the patient's wound with water over which he looks quickly, and almond in his wound.
And then rest for a while; then if the water has descended, then you remove that other time until the almond is thrown.
And then when it is dried and does not descend, then you extract the almond with ease, and roll it with your hand little by little, and then dissolve in the water a little clear salt of gemma and with that wash the wound carefully; and then place outside the wound cotton or a stopper or wool soaked in rose oil and egg white and lick the wound with water.
But in those who are of our time, place on that commi trissat with egg white.
And if you do not obey your almond to the entrance of the wound because of its hardness—because it is some men whose wound is hard very much—then it is necessary that you take the spatula which is called alberid of which this is the form:
And then pierce with that that conjunction, and do not finish your hand in the track, and it is not if you do not make a way to the almond place subtle.
And then introduce the almond according to what we have said.
And you must compliment the work, be prepared to the sleeping patient, made in a dark room, in which he sleeps on his back, and be prohibited from all movements.
And keep in nature to him so that his nature be cleansed, and do not turn his head to the right or left at all.
And be the bandage according to his disposition on the third day.
And then untie that in that dark room and expose the cold sight, and make him see some causes, and then return the bandage on the seventh day.
And do not cover that which you have done at the hour of the cure or soon after the infusion. You must cover that so that the water may gently flow through great and vehement regardment.
But if an abscess occurs, then you must untie the wound before the seventh day, and rectify that with water that yields the abscess.
Then you cover the sight of him and place on his face an oral for which the movement of him be regulated, leaving him for some days, him existing in the dark room.
And then be withdrawn from that room gradually and converse in his causes.
And know that in alchemy the disciple is not excused from vision some times, and then you be bold on the operation.
And already it has come to us of some of those which are in Artach, and some said that they made fire in the Ayrac magdaam perforated with which the water is sucked.
But however, I have not seen in our land any who had perfected water, nor is water written in some of the books of the ancients; and it is possible that this is novel.

Chapter XXIV.
Of the cure of flesh nothing in the nose.
When in the nose are born diverse flesh growths, of which some cause is assembled like a scorpion of moth weight, or a polyp weight; and this malady is called polyp because of the resemblance of that weight represented. And of it is cancerous flesh, pale, of dusky color; and of it is that flesh lion not of dusky color.
Therefore in that which is in these flesh lions not fraudulent nor cancerous, you must make the patient be between your hands and placed in the sun, and dry the nostrils of him, and prick your finger in those flesh. And then extract that to the outer parts, and then incise that which you have comprehended of those with a sharp, subtle spatula from one part, as long as you know that all the flesh is gone; that if any cause of it remains, of which the abscission is possible, then you root that with one of the subtle instruments with ease, as long as none of it remains. But if it bleeds or an abscess occurs, then you pause to him that which you must; or if it is of malignant abscesses, then you cut and cauterize that as long as it is cut and the cavities are all gone.

But if the humidity does not penetrate as it must, then you know that from it is flesh nothing in the pus sobiras bones of the nostrils to which it has not reached abscission.
Therefore then you must introduce a thread of silk into him of which there is some thickness, and weave in it moth nuts, and place between each nut the quantity of the finger or less, and engage the patient and introduce one extremity of the thread into the nostril with the ray or with another cause which is to him possible.

And then place the two extremities of the thread, one extremity that escapes over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and then administer a lock of flesh with the nuts that are in the thread, and do this as long as you know that the flesh is already with the nuts of the thread.
And then extract the thread, and place in the nose after the abstraction of the blood a poultice, and do this for three days or more until the engorged corrodes all that is remaining of the flesh.
And then at the end of the cause, place in the nose a lead pipe for some days until it is healed.

Chapter .xxx.
Of the Extraction of Teeth.
Care that you cure the tooth of its pain with all skill and take your time in the entire extraction of it, for there is no cause that should supplant the healing of it when it is extracted, for it is substance sublime while it is excused in the extraction of it.
May care when the patient is forced that tooth to be extracted, that firmly you must be certain which is the aching tooth, for many times the pain deceives the patient and leads you to believe that it is in a healthy tooth, and you extract that one and then the pain does not cease until the bad and aching tooth is extracted, for we have already seen this by the operation of the barbers.
Therefore, as you must be certain which is the aching tooth, and that you know well, then care that you scarify in the circuit of the tooth with a spatula in which there is some virtue, until it is dissolved from the tooth of the gums of all parts, and then pull that away with your fingers, or with subtle forceps at the beginning little by little until that you succeed.
And then apply a strong hold with large pincers for good communication or great stupor, and place the head of the patient between your teeth that you hold well so that it does not harm, and then pull the tooth according to rectitude in a manner that you do not break that one, nor to the patient greater pain.
And therefore if it is not forgotten, then take one of those instruments, and put that one under it of all parts with facility and exert the removal of it as it was done at the beginning.
But if the tooth is broken or corroded, then care that you compress of cloth that broken and tighten that with the extremity of a subtle ray so that it is not broken in the hour of your constriction upon that with pincers.
And care that you work exquisitely with scarification in the circuit of all parts of the gums and guard much your strength that you do not break that and remain a part of it, and return upon the patient by the malice that it be greater than the first pain of it.
And guard yourself that you do not do what some ignorant barbers do in their fisting and audacity about the extraction of theirs, since they do not administer what we have recommended; for many times they make come upon the men maladies great ones that are more difficult to be broken, and the roots of theirs remaugged all, or some of those, or that you extract that with some bones of the jaw as well as many times we have testified.
And after the extraction of it, the mouth be washed with wine caut or wine agre with salt.
And if it should flow blood for that, as many times it should, then apply some quantity of zegi and sprinkle it over the wound, and if you do not confer that zegi, cauterize.
The form of the forceps and subtle pincers with which the tooth is mauled at the beginning be of long extremity, of short handle and thick, so that they are not bent when you must work with those.
And be as well of thick handle so that when you tighten with those they are not bent, be short extremities.
And be made of Indian iron, descentment made of straight extremities, and in the extremities of those be teeth of which some introne in the others and tighten by strong constriction descent, and some times the extremities of those be the form of the beak of a bird the which has name ciconia, so it is gaunt, and are of strong constriction.

Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of the prominent teeth above the others.
When the teeth are prominent not according to their natural course, then the shape is that, and more so when it befalls women, and more so to the venerable ones; therefore, as you consider: if a tooth is nothing near another tooth, and it is not possible to suture or liniment it, then root that; but that it not be annexed to another tooth, then you incise that with this instrument of which this is the shape; and it is similar to a pig's snout, and be made of Indian iron of a sharp extremity.

Chapter .xxxiii.

Chapter .xxxviii.

And more take an eel and tie it with a thread, and it is placed and  sucked out; or take a porr and suck the ends and suck the in-between.
But if they are not thrown-out with those causes which we have said, then use an instrument of lead according to this form:

And hold its head elevated upwards, and guard yourself that the touching of its bone of the throat, so that it may be dragged to its body and with that which pushes the bone or the thorn, or that the physician with his hand.

Chapter .xxxix.
Of the extraction of sanguisuga annexed to the throat.
When the medicated sanguisuga with that which we have said in the division of the cure with medicines and does not confer, consider then in the throat of the patient to the sun, because you may have comprehended the tongue of it with the instrument which to you we have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the sanguisuga, extract that with a small one or with a subtle gesture decently.
And if it is not to you possible to extract with that, then take a concave canula and introduce that into the throat of the patient, and place in the concavity of the canula a burning iron, and do this as many times (until the sanguisuga is dead and is removed from the throat) and abstain the patient all day of water.
And then chew a berry full of cold water, and work the mouth of it in that, and wash the mouth with that; and do not swallow any of that cause and evil the water one hour after with its hand, because the sanguisuga as soon as it feels the water catz.
But if it is not thrown-out with that which we have recommended, then subfumigate the patient with cimet or with asafoetida by the instrument which we have recommended in the subfumigation of the uvula.
Do this, so that it falls.
And it is another manner of operation in the subfumigation of that, is that you take a bowl in which there are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a cover in the middle of which there is a hole, and it is composed in that hole the extremity of the instrument; and then let go from below the subfumigation; and place the patient its mouth at the extremity of the canula, and close its mouth so that the subfumigation is not thrown-out until you know that the subfumigation has arrived at the sanguisuga, because the sanguisuga as soon as it falls.
And if it does not fall, then you iterate the subfumigation many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and eat salty causes and herbs, and do not drink water, and thus necessary is that with this regimen be thrown-out.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the sanguisuga of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it is similar to forceps as you see, unless that in it there is some curvature: Which is placed in the throat, and the extremity of it is similar to the beak of a stork, which is gaunt, in which it is aspired of lime, so that, when compressing any cause, it does not let go.
Chapter .xl.
In which is the sum of the discourse concerning abscesses and their section.
Abscesses are certain special kinds, of certain manners, according to what we remember of them, of each one in this book.
And they are diverse in their piercing and sectioning by two manners, of which one is by the species of abscesses in themselves; and by that which we understand of the humidities.
And the second manner is according to the places where they occur in the body, for the abscess that occurs in the head is another from the abscess that occurs in the buttock; and the abscess in the fleshy place is another from the abscess that occurs in the joint; and to each of them is its own play by operation.
And more than abscesses are some of which it is necessary that they not be perforated, but until the maturation of the pus in them or the completion of them.
There are other abscesses which it is necessary to lance when they are ripe, and not until their completion, such as abscesses that are near the joints, for when an abscess is near a joint, its being is prolonged until it can reach what is in the circuit of it, and then its ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, so that it causes a contraction of that limb; or it is an abscess near the main member, and if you delay the perforation of it until it is ripe, it will harm the main member; or it is near the buttock, therefore perforate it before it is ripe; and do not perforate it crude, for lack of proper digestion, but that which is near the buttock, so that you do not pierce its prepuce and make it elongate to the parts of the buttock, and make a fistula, or that it is done at the edge of it that it is not healed. But you must know the hour of the abscess's perforation, and that is when it is ripe.
And you must know that it is ripe when there is the cessation of pain and the cessation of fever, and near the diminution of the heat and the pulse, and the sharpness of the head of the abscess, and the other signs.
And that you must know the perforation to be done in the place pus after the abscess and pus coming from the cure of the eminence.
And the perforation should always be done along the length of the flesh or the body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the limbs or the feet, and in the places of the tendons, of the nerves, of the arteries; and, lastly, in all equal places in which there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use the perforation according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the perforation of it until its digestion is confirmed according to its completion, as we have said; for if you perforate it before that, it prolongs the course of its power and a lot of dirt, and then the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it.
But some abscesses are perforated according to the latitude of the flesh or the body according to necessity, or according to what the limb needs.
And you must administer a small perforation, and in large abscesses a large perforation and many sections according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And others are of abscesses in which it is necessary that the wound be concave and be inclosed, when it is done so that it is like bread and is done at the edge that it already sticks, as those that occur in clusters of boils and buboes.
And of those there are that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those there is one in which it is incised like the figure of a myrtle leaf, as the abscesses of the angles.
And of those there are those in which a round section and a lunar section are administered, and similar to those.
But that one to whom there is no such as his abscesses are superficial, you must perforate that with a superficial perforation, or flat only.
And you must, when the abscess is large and has already collected a lot of pus, perforate it and do not try to extract all the pus in that hour; having extracted one part, and then close the abscess until the next day, and then extract a larger part, and so do this several times according to the degree until it is completely drained.
And most of all if the patient is of frail virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old person in decrepitude, for the animal spirit is often resolved with the egress of the pus, and then the patient dies easily, and you operate on them.
But guard this chapter with great care, and in the perforation of these abscesses, you must cleanse the wounds and consider therefore whether the plague of the abscess is little, or a flat section, then you administer the poultices of it or of a counter-poultice; and if the abscess is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, then you must place a bandage on each one until they meet.
And if in the abscess a part of the wound is abscised or has been concaved in the circuit, then you must cover it with a poultice of old cloth or a thread made of linen of it, as when you have treated loaves or roots, its moisture; and strengthen that on the third day; and then process that and cure it with what is necessary until it is healed.
But if blood flows during the operation, then you administer cold water and wine in which you have soaked a cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
But if the bleeding persists, then you must administer regimen and cure, and powders as I have recommended in many places in this our book and division.
But if it is in winter, and the place of the abscess is a place of many nerves, then you must cover it with powders in wine and hot oil, and place them on the spot.
And if it is in summer, and the places are fleshy, then you must place powders soaked in water and oil, or in wine and oil, and all that be hot until the third day, as we have said, and then you must open the abscess and cleanse it and administer to it what is necessary for its healing until it is cured.
And thus is what is necessary for the knowledge of the cure of abscesses universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of all abscesses in what manner is the way of their cure by chapters individually.
Chapter .xli.
Of the incision of abscesses which come in the nape of the neck.
In the nape of the neck small abscesses, and so of species of nodes which contain tunics that are to their making; and the species of them are many.

And in the incision of all, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as you must the exteccio of those does not make contrary artery.
And the operation in incision of those is that you probe those with an instrument the shape of which comes near thus, which is called entromes, as long as you know that it contains.
Because if that which contains is humidity, then you split that with incision according to the length by superficial incision according to this form:
And begins in the incision of the line of .B. into the line of .G. Therefore, as the humidity is evacuated, then you excoriate that skin which contains that humidity, and do not leave of that any cause of all, because troops many times return, if there remain of that any cause.
And then you submerge the wound in Egyptian poultice, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill with that the sore and leave it for another day, because with that you corrode all that is raw of that pellicle.
And then iterate over that wound with Egyptian poultice second and third times if you judge it necessary, until that you are confident that there is no raw any cause of that pellicle; then cure the sore with poultice until it is healed.
And if the abscess contains fatty nodes, then you incise that according to this form: with incision having the shape of a cross, and get oncis between two lips of the incision and scrape that from all parts, and exert your strength in the extraction of the tunic which contains that.

And similarly do in the stony abscess of incision and cure according to what I have told you; and incision over stony abscess is easier, because it is of little blood and of little humidity.
And sometimes there are some of these abscesses which are in the head in some men with whom there is no humidity at all; the cause of which is because I incised over an abscess in the head of an old woman and brought back the abscess thus as a hard, rough, white sore, which could not be drained, and if someone was struck with that, it would cause them a plague.
But in the other abscesses accidents in the head other than this is not this chapter, as the abscesses which come to the heads of children and you must the roots of the ears, but the incision of all these is superficial incision.

Chapter .xlii.
Of the incision of scrofulas which happen in the neck.
Many times these abscesses become in the neck and in the armpits and in the groin; and sometimes they happen in the other parts of the body.
And they are those that happen in the neck, and they are many that are generated between them, and all scrofula of those is within its own tunic, and as in the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have recounted.
And the species of these scrofulas are many, because of those some are stony, and of those some contain humidity, and of those are malignant the ones which do not obey to cure.
Therefore in that which you see of good disposition in the Touch, of which the color of that which is manifest is proper to the color of the neck, and is mauled to all parts, and is not annexed to the nerve of the neck, nor to the veins, nor to the artery, and is not pre-owned, then you must incise that with superficial incision from the lower part to the upper part of the body of the line of .G. into the line of .B., and scrape that from all parts, and extend the lips of the neck with onci, or with many oncis if you have need of those, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract that little by little.
And it is more caution that the vein or nerve is not incised.
And let the spatula not be too sharp, so that you do not cut your hand, or that you wound the patient, and that you cut what is not necessary to cut; for if you were to cut a vein or artery and prohibit yourself from your operation, then put in the place a trite vitriol or other powders that cause the flow of blood, and tighten the wound, and leave that inside which rests the sharpness of the abscess and the wound is softened and begins to be pus. When the blood is drawn.
Therefore, return to your operation before you have completed it.
And then inquire with your finger if there is any cause of other small abscesses, therefore cut those and cleanse them.

And then fill the wound with old cotton which you have already submerged in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
And if you cut that abscess entirely, then cover it so that you adjust the two lips of the wound and close it as soon as pus is released so that there is no superfluous residue.
But if you see that there is superfluous residue due to the size of the abscess, cover it so that you understand to cut the root of it, and extract it and administer suturing and what is said.
And those of the abscesses that contain humidity, perforate it with a superficial perforation where you see the place of maturation of it, and place a perforation that lets the pus flow from the bottom of the body, as we have said.
And then administer perforation,  ointments and similar things to those, so that it corrodes what is left of the corruption. And then when you see the wound already cleansed, then cure it with ointment of generative flesh until it is healed.
Chapter .xliii.
Of the section of the abscess of the pile within the gullet.
The ancients said this section in the pile, and no one in our land has done it.
And this is the inscription of the sermon of those.
But in men having a hernia, cover that it be avoided the extraction of the pile, as for that it is not well done because all the veins and major arteries of the body are here.
But in those who have abscesses caused in the mouth or gullet or two ears, when the illness is not in the canal, cover using the section of the pile to escape the destruction which is done by perforation.
Therefore, when we want this, cover that they cut the pile below three circles of the circles of the pile, or four with a small section for the latitude in that which is between two circles for quantity, that the section be in the flesh, not in the cartilage, and this place is convenient for section, because it is deprived of flesh and the blood vessels of it are there.
And if the doctor is fearful, cover that he extends the cord of the gullet with an onion, and then fends the cord until it reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if he sees any cause of them.
And then cut the flesh as we have recounted; and it is signified over the section of the canal by the flame which is of that issued with that which is of its disruption and by the abscess of the voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore, as the hour is remaugded in which perforation is feared, add two lips of the cord of the wound, and sew that alone as the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that make flesh grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis says that the sum of the sermon which we have recounted, the exposition is not but to see that some of these abscesses have already opened the gullet of the patient, and the patient has come to death, and the throat of it is dried up, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient breathes over the place of the wound by some respiration, and be saved from death.
And for that, we command to leave the wound open until the malice of the illness is consumed; and the malice of it is for three days; and then cover the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And what I have seen with my own eyes, is that a servant took a knife and put it in her gullet and cut with it a part of the canal of the lung, and I was called to the cure of it, and I returned the woman as she was moaning of the dying, and I uncovered the wound and returned the blood which was issued from the wound small.
Therefore, I was confessed that she had not cut a vein or artery, and the wind was issuing from the wound, and I cured it until it was healed.
And I did not accuse the servant if she did not worsen in the voice, and after some days, she returned to the improvement of her dispositions.
And now I say that in the section of the ephialtes there is no fear.
Chapter XLIV.
Of incision over an abscess which occurs in the throat outside, and is called a hernia of the throat.
This abscess called a hernia of the throat is a large abscess according to the color of the body, and it moves in women.
And it is according to two manners, whether it is natural or accidental.
And in the natural one it is not a matter of curing.
And the accidental one is according to two manners, of which one is similar to fatty nodes, and the other manner is similar to an abscess which is made by a blockage of an artery, and in that one there is fear. And no one should make presumption about it as if it were iron, but only in the one that is small. And then you should examine that one with the finger, and if you find it similar to a fatty node, and it is not suspended by any of the veins, then you should incise it like the nodes, and extract it with that which contains it from the skin and bursa; and if not, then you should scrutinize its entire being, and then care for the place with what is necessary for healing before it is healed.
Chapter XLV.
Of incision of the species of nodes.
Of nodes there are many species, and I have already said all the species of them in the division.
And I should recount thus the difference between a node and an excrescence as if making a doubt.
Therefore, I say that in an excrescence there is heat and fever and vehement pains until the boiling of the superfluity is subdued; and it is completed by putrefaction that at the hour the fever, the pain, and the heat cease.
But in a node there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that which is a lion's head which is in the u sac proper.
And it is according to the color of the body, and the beginning of it is like a cyst and is made so as a vase, whether it is larger or smaller, and they are according to two species, whether they are fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, according to what I said in the division.
Therefore, when you arrive at the cure of a node, that you should examine it and inquire about it at the beginning with the instrument which is called intromes, according to how it will come to its form in the chapter which is near this one.
And the manner of inquiry of abscesses and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it into the place most humid which you find in the abscess, and you will revolve your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the core.
And then lastly, your hand according to the measure of the greatness of the abscess, and then extract the intromes and consider what is emitted in the trace of it.
And if the humidity is flowing out, of whatever color it may be, then you should incise it with a superficial incision according to what I have said in the other abscesses.
And if from the trace of the intromes there is no humidity, then you should know that it is fatty.
And make a dry incision over it having the form of a cross according to this form: as I have taught you, and suspend that with tweezers, and excoriate the core from all parts with ease, and guard the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sania with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract that sania, and many times it must be so, and then you extract it in pieces until from it there remains no cause.
Because if from it remains no cause, little or much, the node returns according to the most.
And if you see that from it remains any small part, then complete the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and strengthen the wound, and place over it which sits abscess caut, and cure that of the other healing until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you stitch the two lips of it and cure that with what encases.
But if a pulsating vein is to it contrary, or non-pulsating, then you coat and moisten the place with zegi trissat which is vitriol and leave it straight for two days or three until you can pierce the wound and that the boiling of the blood rests; and then return to incise what is broken from the node.

Chapter .xlvii.
Of the cure of the nipples of men which are assembled from women.

Chapter .xlviii.

Chapter .xlix.
Of the incision of abscesses that occur due to artery or vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the tissue that is on top of it is consolidated, then often abscesses occur. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are due to the artery or vein: that when an abscess is due to the artery, it is long attached to the front of the body; and that when you pierce the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it a kind of stridor.
And that which is due to the vein is round and manifest on the front of the body.
And the incision on this abscess is an error, and most of all in that which is below the armpits, and in the angles, and in the neck, and in many places of the body; and it is very large, therefore, that its cure with iron should be avoided, and that which is in the extremities, or on the head, should be avoided.
But over that which is of them due to inflammation of the orifice of the artery, dissect in the tissue a long incision; and then scrape the incision with forceps and then the artery, and deliurate of the tunics until it is uncovered.
And then place on that needle and make it penetrate into the other side, and tighten the artery with a double thread in two places, — which causes you to see the extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And then pierce the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula until the blood that is in it is removed, and the abscess is dissolved.
And then administer a cure in which it is generated power until the ligaments fall; and then care for it with suitable ointments to that until it is healed.
And if the abscess is due to the section of a vein, then you must have with your hand that which is possible of the abscess with the tissue, and then introduce the needle below the place which you have had below your hand, and make it penetrate; and be in that double thread until you extract that from the other side, and then ligate the abscess with a good ligament according to what I have told you in the ligament of uva4 of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that the thread will be extracted, then introduce the thread with that needle below the entire abscess, with the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
Then dry the abscess in the middle place of it until when it is emptied of what is in it, then you dissect the superfluity of the tissue, and leave what of it is tied.
And then place on it the powder which you have submerged in wine and oil, and then administer the cure which is made with calques and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 1 of the abscess which occurs due to a twisting of nerves.
Thus as abscesses occur in arteries and veins, and similarly abscesses occur in nerves when they are struck or worked too much, and similarly.
And it is made most in the places of the assistants or the talus, or in any place where the joints are sore.
And it is a serious abscess, and it is assembled to the color of the other body, and in the majority of its dispositions, it is surrounded by them, and when it is squeezed with violence, the patient feels in it a semblance of stupor.
And it is not an abscess added in the front of the body, and for this, the chain is left, and it is sore in every part and does not go to the front or back parts.
Therefore, those that are in the joints should not be enveloped with iron, for it will certainly cause contraction.
But the one that is in the head or in the front, close the chain with a spatula. But if it is a small abscess, then take that with the forceps and cut it from the root.
And if it is large, then suspend it with an anchor, and excise it, and then cover it; and adjust the bandage with sutures, and cure it until it is healed.
Chapter .li.
Of the section of an abscess which occurs from a boil that occurs to the belly.
And it happens to some men, boils on their bellies and in other parts of their bodies, of which some are called fungous because of their resemblance to fungi, of which the root is thin and the head is thick; and already the lips of these are turned, and some are small, and some are greatly magnified.
And I have already seen one, and in the belly of him there were two parts which were more like fungi, and there was no difference between those white, of fine root.

And if the midwife skillfully and makes what is done with ease and subtlety, and with delay, and is ingenious according to all figure according to what is prepared for her by the art leading to health.
Remembrance of it that is formed in the womb from embryos and are aborted.
Sometimes they are formed in the womb one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, and sometimes ten, and it has already been verified that one woman aborts six, and another ten, all of which is caused by the measurement of the glorious wise.
And all this cove that is in the science of the midwife, because it is very useful to that appearance of this, and therefore it is paused to this as much as cove.
