Of extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of the medicine and it is not outside emitted, and you are forced to use of operation with hand, then cove that you consider if the woman is of healthy virtue and is not with any of the accidents by which she is feared for perdition.
Then cove that the woman be laid on the sheet over her two, and be the head of her inclined downwards and the thighs of her be elevated.
And the minister have those of two parts or be tied in the sheet so that the body of him no extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mouth of the mother of him with humid oils and with mucellage of altea and of fenugrec and of seed of lily.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucellages, and then introduces her hand with facility in the mother, and then seeks with the hand in the place in which the fetus lies.
And convenient places in this: therefore you consider if the fetus is prepared that descends over its head, and then you place the uncis in the heels of it, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or behind the beard, or in the fork of it, or in the proper places of the back, or behind the hypochondria.
More if the descent is over the feet of it, then in the pentinilh, or in the middle of the back.
And cove that he have the unci with the right hand, and pause the curvature of it in that place the which is between the fingers of the left hand, and introduces the hand with facility and place the unci in some of those places the which we have said, until it reaches the left cause.
And then pause and place in the opposite position of it another unci, or the third if it is necessary, so that the traction be equal, and not be extension according to its rectum only.
And be maugut to all part, so that the emission of it be alleviated as it is done during the eradication of it.
And cove in it that which is between them that the extension be mollified; and if any part of it is retained, then cove that the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and introduces those expertly and revolves with those that are retained.
Therefore if the part of the fetus is out-gotten, then the uncis are changed into the place which is most high; and do so until all the fetus is out-gotten.
But if the hand is issued before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it by the constriction of it, then cove that a cloth be enveloped over it; and then extracts it until all is out-gotten, and incides it either in the junction of the hand or in the groin.
And thus cove that you do in the other hand and in the two feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is constriction in the emission, or there is water adjusted in the head of it, then cove that you introduce between the fingers of the scapula and split the head and extract the water, or what describes this with an instrument which is called "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of the other instruments in the chapter which is next to this.
And similarly do if the fetus is of large head by nature: and then cove that you incides it with the algematu, or that you press it with the alunda as we have said; and then extract the bones with the forceps.
And if the head is issued and is constricted by the fork, then it be split until the humidity which is in the feet be poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obese, then you cut the head as soon as it is possible to you.
And if the folds of the belly are abscesses or are in it hydrophic, then you must pierce that within which flows the humidity that is in it.
But if the fact is on their feet, then the attraction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the mother is lighter.
But if it is constricted of the belly and the foot, then you must extract that with a cloth which you will have enveloped over your hand, and that you make the belly and the foot within which runs that which is in those.
But if the other members are held and the head returns, then the metron inserts her left hand; but if the mouth of the mother is closed, then she inserts her hand into the preon of her, and seeks with that the head, and pulls that with her fingers into the mouth of the mother, and then inserts into it a hook, or two hooks, and pulls it with those.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted by an abscess caused by a cautery that has fallen on it, then you must not tremble over it; rather, you must administer an infusion of humid fatty causes. And administer plasters; and follow the patient in waters that soften and moisten.
And if the fact is on their side, then if possible, it should be lanced; and it should be administered with the water that we have said in the living fact.
And if that is not possible, then it should be incised in pieces, and extracted.
And you must not leave any cause of the second kind.
And when you will have completed all your operation, then administer the water that we have said of the cure in the cauterized abscesses which have fallen on the mother.
And if there occurs a flux of blood, then send them down in styptic waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in the belly of which was a dead fetus, and then above that fire another pregnancy, and then the dead fetus is another. It happened to a man a long time ago an abscess in his navel; and it inflated so much that it opened, and began to discharge pus.
And I was called to the cure of him, and medicated him for a long time, and the plague was not consolidated.
Then I placed on him some causes of strong attraction plasters, and extracted from him a bone, and after passing some days, and extracted another bone; and I was too amazed, as in the belly there were no bones.
And then I thought that they were of the bones of the dead fetus.
Therefore I continued to treat the abscess, and extracted from it many bones, the woman existing in her usual dispositions, and already living in that manner for a long time, cured of it a little pus.
And I do not affirm that this is strange, but that in this there is science and help to that which the physician performs with his hand for the cure.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of a vertigue with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of a stretcher in which the boards are joined, to the joining of which are two vertigues in two extremities of two boards. But however this vertigue must be more subtle of strictori, and be made either of ebony or of wood of boys.
And it should be the width of each stick two fingers, and the margin of each one is one finger, and the length of each one is one palm and a half; and in the middle place of two sticks are two adjustments of that same stick, which are already finished, of which the length is the majority of one palm and a little more, and the width of each one is two fingers, or a little less.
And these two additions are inserted into the mouth of the mother so that it may be opened with those when you revolve the two prescribed vertigues.
Another form similar to that more subtle and lighter:
It is made of ebony or wood sticks according to the resemblance of forceps. But however, at the extremity of it are two additions as if it were, and the length of those additions is about one palm, and the width of each one is two fingers.
And as you want to open the mother with those, then you make the woman lie on her back with her feet dangling, open that which is between her thighs. And then open your hand with the instrument as if you were doing with forceps, accordingly to the quantity that you want of the opening of the mouth of the mother until the metron makes it so that you want.

Of the extraction of the secondine.
When the secondine is retained in childbirth, then you command the woman to retain her breath, and then make her to strain with condition, and strengthen your hand over her mouth and over her nostrils, and if by this it is brought forth, it is good.
And if not, then you take a cloth and perforate in the cover a hole and place in that herbs burning in the mouth of the mother, thus as calament and rue and anise and chamomile and sicados arabic and cinnamon and centaury. All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the cloth, and place that over the fire.
And then place a tube of cane in the mouth of the mother, and keep that inside so that the vapor comes to the cavity of the mother.
And then make her to strain as we have said, and the secondine is ejected with velocity.
But if this cure remains and it is not brought forth, then you command the midwife to submerge her left hand in sesame oil or in a mixture of althea, and then introduce that into the vagina and search with that for the secondine, and when she has found it, then she takes it and extends it little by little. But if it is attached in the perineum of the mother, then she introduces her hand as we have recounted, and when she has found the secondine, she extracts it little by little according to rectum so that the mother does not suffer violent traction. It is necessary that it be changed to the right and left sides with facility.
And if the mouth of the mother is constricted, we have already recounted the cure with straining and with medication of the cloth with herbs.
But if it is not brought forth with all the causes that we have recounted, then guard yourself that you do not tire over it in iteration of abstraction, but rather that what is brought forth from it to the mouth of the mother lies on the cloth of the woman, and then sterilize that with an enguent and tetrafarmacon; for this will cause it to rot a little after a few days and it will be dissolved and it will be brought forth.
But when it can be done, it is elevated to the head and stomach, and this is what the woman feels; and therefore it is necessary that fumigations and conveniences be administered to it.
But some of the Ancients already were using fumigations of mastic and dried figs.
Way to make an instrument with which the woman is fumigated for the retention of menstruation and of the secondine:
It is made of  wood or of iron.
And it is placed with the subtle extremity in the vagina and the wide extremity over the fire, and the fumigation is placed over the embers of the fire.
And keep that inside so that the fumigation is consumed and iterate another.
Of the cure of the un-perforated child's anus.
Many children are born and their anuses are not perforated, those which are very subtle and opalescent. Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to perforate with her finger that opalescent; and if not, perforate it with a sharp spatula, and guard yourself that it does not touch the sphincter.
And then place on it wool infused in wine and oil; and then cure it with an enguent until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is opalescent, then place in the hole a tube for many days, and remove it when the child wants to defecate.
And already accidents opalescence of the anus by consolidation of plague or of abscess; therefore, it is necessary that that consolidation be incised, and then it be cured with what we have said of the cure and of the lead.
Of the cure of fistulas that come from the bowels.
The fistulas that come from the part of the bowels, low, so knotted and thick, those that come from near the anus outside or in the space of the one part.
And it is a fistula or many.
And as that knot is ancient and flows from the humid white or subtle rot, and sometimes in these fistulas some penetrate.
And those that penetrate are known by what is brought forth from them by the egress and by the windiness; and sometimes the woman of egress, and very often it is brought forth from them worms.
And some of those fistulas sometimes penetrate into the space, into the bladder, and into the meat of the vagina; and some of these penetrate into the junction of the groin and into the knot of the hip.
And in what is known as a fistula penetrating into the anus and not penetrating, is that you put your finger inside the anus, and you try to insert a thin probe of wax or iron into the fistula when there is no blockage.
But if there is a blockage in that, then you insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair into it until you feel the probe or hair in your finger.
And if you don't feel that at all, nor does any cause of stool, worm, or wind come from the tract, thus as we have said, then you know that it is not penetrating, and then you turn to its cure.
And when the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the meat of the vagina, then the meaning of it is the emission of urine from that and prohibition of it so that the place may be consolidated with medicine.
But if it is penetrating into the junction of the groin or into the hip and there is a feeling of pain in the area, then the sign of it is that the probe penetrates here if there is no blockage in it into the hip, and a feeling of pain in the area of the groin; and that it always brings a discharge; and that it doesn't work in that medicine, nor is it consolidated with rinsing.
And in all of those fistulas, there is no cure for all, and the cure for them is the work and variety of the physician's leaves upon which it is based.
But in that which is not penetrating and not ancient, healing with iron is expected according to what I tell you, and what I have already tried.
And it is that the patient lays between your hands on his two and elevates his legs into them, the thighs being inclined to his belly, and then you insert a probe of lead, or wax if there is a blockage in the fistula, until you know the location where the probe penetrates.
And if that feels the patient around the buttock, then cover that you insert your finger inside the buttock.
And if you feel in your finger the probe already by itself penetrating, or another that you feel between your finger and that skin or flesh, then you know certainly that it is penetrating; and therefore don't work on that, for it is not in that healing, as we have said.
But nevertheless, some say that it is healed in some men tart.
And of the medicine by which healing is expected in it is that you ignite a subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as it is preceded, and insert that ignited into the fistula until it reaches around the buttock; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all of those flesh adjusted to the fistula, that are similar to the feather quill of a bird, are already cauterized.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border until all of those flesh that are cauterized are covered, and then cure that with medicines that generate and consolidate the flesh, and if it is healed, well is; and if not, then it is not healed in any time by other cure.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate into your finger which is in the buttock, and between that and the probe which is veiled with skin or flesh, and sometimes the fistula in that which seizes the surface of the buttock, then dry the buttock from the beginning of the fistula, and you see drying with the probe, and it is in the fistula until the drying reaches the place where the extremity of the probe reaches, and by the probe it is liberated and caught.
And then purify those fistula-ridden flesh, which are assembled like the feather quill of a bird, and do not remain any cause from them.
But if a flux of blood sometimes comes between you and your operation when you are cauterizing those flesh, then the best that is, and of the lightest instrument is to cauterize with fire or with acute medicine, for cauterizing with fire adjusts good two habits: it is the cauterization of those flesh adjusted, and the abscessing of the blood, the excretion of the humidities.
And then cure that with poultices wrapped in border or in tripe until the place gets braced, and then cure the plague with rinses of hard flesh-generating and consolidating.
And so medicines in which there is astringency and excretion; when then it is restored, it is already healed and you fear no iteration.
But if the fistula already reaches into the front of the buttock and is elongated from its surface to the body, then insert your finger into the buttock and inquire with that.
And therefore if you feel the probe and between you and it is veiled with flesh or skin, and it is proper to penetration, then it is not an operation in it but according to your trust and hope.
The which cause is to administer in it one of three ways: or that you cauterize it as we have said; or that you dry it until you obtain the concavity of it so that it is possible for you to insert the probes and the proper cure; and do not proceed to cut it so that you do not cut the ligament containing the buttock, and which happens over the patient in the emission of the stool by his will; and then cure that with what we have said that strong leeches heal; or that you lengthen that veil and cleanse that pus that dries that within the buttock, as we have said, or with a probe or another instrument of sharp extremity, and then purify those fistula-ridden flesh which are in the incision where you can make a percussive; and then strive to make the restoration of the whole plague with incision, and if the orifice of pus above is not consolidated, and the fistula remains open in the part of the buttock, and pus light remains for the patient. And sometimes the fistula is finished in this way: when you introduce the probe into the fistula, and it is in the place of the anus around the surface of the body with the chain and on the edge of the anus, then take a probe of perforated extremity, which is like a needle of preparing the hearts according to this form:
And introduce it into that faithful envelope of v threads or around those; and then introduce the probe with thread into the fistula until you achieve its cavity.
But if it is penetrating in the edge of the anus near the entrance, then you extract the thread from that tract so that you introduce your finger into the anus; and extract the extremity of the thread and adjust the two extremities simultaneously, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or two, and when you have incised the thread deeper into the flesh, tighten well that which those flesh parts are incised between the two extremities of the thread and that they join.
And then cure the plague while it is consolidated and healed.
But if the orifice of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate, in whatever way it is prepared, but not that it is moved in the groin, because it is not to you that you should do this so that you do not cut the tendon; and then make it with that until it is healed.
The shape of the spatula spines with which the fistula is cut: the curvature of which is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that you do not cut what is not necessary, as sometimes.
Of stitching hemorrhoids in which blood flows in the incision of those.
Hemorrhoids are in two ways, which are between the anus similar to those that are of carbon, or which those are like the fat of a raisin. And of those are small and large, and that the blood flows from those always and is one, and are many, and are outside the anus, and in the extremities of it.
But however, those that are outside the anus are according to the little moisture, of which flows a little water or a little blood with a continuous body, and are according to the color of the body.
And the cure of those that are inside the anus is that you command the patient to squat and to squeeze until the anus is empty and the hemorrhoids appear to you. Then you take and suspend with hooks or whatever you have those with your finger, and then cut those deeply to their roots.
But if the hooks are not held in those because of the moisture of them and their softening, then take those with rough cloth or with a stick or with wool fleece, and extract those with your fingers, and then cut those and pulverize upon them some powders caudas near the incision, so that they are applied to those in place of cauterization; or cauterize those according to what is preceded in the chapter of cauterization. And then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey the egress, then cauterize the patient with cauteries in which there is a small bite, and wash it with that water that is in the anus and that obeys the egress slightly when the patient is squeezed.
But if the hemorrhoids are outside the anus, then the cause of them is lighter, and it is that you take those with your finger, or that you take those with a hook, and cut those, and then cure those with the water that we have said until they are healed.
And that which you have incised, cover that you administer suture of them according to this way: take thread enveloped and introduce it into a needle and then extract the hemorrhoids to the upper parts, and make it penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and encircle the two extremities of the thread in the part farthest from the needle, and it is laterally; and tighten the hemorrhoid with strong structure, and then knot the thread and extract the needle.
And do this to all, and leave one of those and do not stitch it, so that the superfluity of the blood flows from that.
And then place on the anus cloth soaked in rose oil or in cerot; and place that on the anus and command the patient to rest. And then leave that until it heals; and when it is healed, cure those with poultices or with other cure until it is healed.
And as they are ancient and do not work in that medicine, then you must scrape those with the point of the spatula or with your finger until they are made humid and there is a host of those the pus below, which prohibits those from consolidation; and then cure those until they are consolidated.
Then you open those with a reason of pus vehement that the first one until there is much blood and they are excoriated; and then cure those until they are healed.
Know that almesamir, it is called, and it is nothing but a red knot according to the color of the body resembling the head of a clavicle, and it is made in all the body and mostly in the parts below the feet and in the fingers, and therefore by those pains the ailment.
And therefore, the one that is incised that which is in the circuit of the key, and it is held with the forceps or with an awl, and it is eradicated from its root; and then care for that.
And if you wish, cauterize the second that precedes in its chapter.
But of wart is a small, rough, fistulous, round eminence on the surface of the body, and many times they come in the hands of children.
And the cure of it is that you extend and cut that, or that you tighten that with a thread or with a needle that is put inside that. And if you wish, cauterize that, according to what we have said, with fire or with acute medicine.
But the ant hill is a small, fetid or fistulous eminence on the surface of the body, going to the pain, and when the ant finds that it is felt in it, seeming like a bite of an ant, and it is made around the body.
And the cure of it is that you take a tube of hawk feather or of vulture feather, and it is strong, and you place that over the ant hill while you contain it the circle of the tube from the parts of it; and then you turn your hand with the tube while you cut that which is in the circuit of the ant hill, and you place that in the skin of the flesh, and that you eradicate the ant hill from its root.
And if you wish, do that with a tube of brass or of iron according to this form:
Let the part above the tube be drawn to subtlety, deaf (so it is not perforated), enveloped so that over the said, the apprehension of it be abated and the revolution of that.
And if you wish, cauterize the ant hill according to what is said before in the cauterization of the boil in the chapter of cauteries.

Of the cure of the plagues.
And I have already said in the division of the cure of the plagues what was convenient to the book, and I say thus the cure of those with my hand and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore I say that the plagues are diversified according to what in which they are made the plagues and according to the place on which fall the plagues.
And the causes for which many times are made the plagues so as by a blow of a stone, or incision of a sword or of a spear, or percussion with a lance, or with a club, or with an arrow, or similes to those of many causes.
But the plagues that are in the places of the body are like the plague that falls upon the head, or the neck, or the feet, or the belly, or the arm, and resemble those of the limbs.
And you are considering the cure of some plagues so that you pause that reasoning and rule over the other plagues.
And you begin with the plagues of the head simple, because the remembrance of the composed will come at the beginning of the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple plague occurs in the head and it is not a fracture, then consider: if it is due to a gem or a similar thing, and the bone has been broken only slightly and it is a large plague and you fear a boil on that patient, then you take care and immediately perform cephalic flebotomy, and do not delay this; and extract from that of the blood according to the quantity of its virtue, if no other cause prohibits flebotomy, especially if the blood that is drawn from the plague is little.
And it is the flebotomy of the opposite side of the afflicted part; and guard the patient from repletion and from wine and from heavy food.
But if from the little [amount of blood] some cause prohibits, then let the food be lessened and do not approach meat nor wine.
And place on the plague, if a boil occurs there, a cloth infused in rose oil or in wine in which is stippled.
But if it is certain of a boil, then place on the plague, if it is recent, its blood and the air has not changed that powder which I will recommend soon.
And if the air has already changed that, then place on [a poultice] of herbs until it is healed.
But if the plague is large or is due to a cut of space and similar things, and the lips of it are not adjusted by sutures, then adjust those with sutures according to what I will recommend of the sutures of them.
But if the plague is already uncovered of the bone and skin, and it is not a retention of it but a small suspensory, then incise that and then cure the plague with medicines and restore the flesh to the place of the bone, and command the patient to be cautious of foods in which there is heaviness: caps and forms cooked and similar to them, until it is composed.
And if it rots in the bone and does not adhere to the bone, then you incise all that pus and throw it out, and then cure that.
But if in these plagues an artery or vein from which blood flow can come, and it is not severed by medicines, then you inquire about the artery, and if you find that not incise, then you incise that with a spatula, or cauterize it; and if necessity provokes that what we have said does not confer, then you cauterize until the blood is severed.
And if these plagues are simple and small, then the cause of them is light;  in this way that you pulverize on those this powder, because consolidated that before the air changes them.
And the manner of the powder is this: receive olive oil, one part, of dragon's blood, two parts, of cautery, three parts; all be ground and sifted, and of this, fill the plague, and be constricted by good constriction until it well adheres on it, and be coagulated with the blood.
And then strengthen that with poultices and leave it, and do not unbind it while it is thus, so that no medicine is extracted from it until it is healed.
And some times do this alone cautery, when it is not to you in present olive oil and dragon's blood.
And already do this same operation in the great plagues when it convenes that it be placed on those and they be tightened, and so plagues recent with their blood, which the air has not altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially when it is in summer time, then it is not understood in the position of this powder, but rather cure those with what we have said, in this way that you place on those some digested herbs, or that you place on those powder of barley flour with water and honey until they get a poultice; and then cure those with the other cure until they are healed.
But if a plague occurs with a fracture in the bone, and it is small, then you extract that with a  [surgical] instrument.
And I say the cure of the fractures of the head in that which is venomous.
Of the plagues of the neck.
But if the plague occurs in the neck, then there is no difference in medication, and between the plague of the head when it is simple.
But if the nerve of the neck is incised or the artery, then if it is a nerve, it is not in it, but that its cure with what does vehement cauterization is avoided, like ziniar and zegi that is vitriol and similar to them because they are harmful to the nerves and contract that. And do not place on the plague any cause of all cold, because the substance of the nerves is cold and the continuation of it is with the brain, which is the most delicate of all the members.

Of the cure of  fistula and abscess.
Know that every hernia and abscess when it is inflamed and gets old, and is made an ulcer, and is not consolidated and throws out pus all the time and is not cut off, then, in whatever member it may be, universally it is called a fistula and we call that one a zuchem.
And fistula according to truth is a fibrous, hard, white nodule, with which there is no pain and which has a concavity like the concavity of a bird's bone; and for this reason, that one is called by some "rizatz", that is, bone.
And it is in some men moist, the one that throws out pus; and very quickly the moisture is cut off in some hours. And sometimes this moisture is moved, and it is little, and it is thick, and it is subtle.
I have already shown all those causes, and their symptoms and the cure of them with medicines in the division.
And therefore I want to make you know the cure of fistula which is done by the way of operation with the hand.
And know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for some of these are fistulas that reach the large veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the brain, or the intestine, or the bladder, or any of the ribs, or any of the vertebrae of the spine, or any of the joints composed by composition as if from the hand and the foot; and of these, those that give to it proximity of the principal member and of resemblances.
And therefore of these fistulas that are according to this manner are of the diseases of difficult healing, and no receive cure, and occupation with that is work and ignorance.
And if it is of the fistulas some the depth of which does not reach these places that have been said, and you wait and trust in the cure of it, and you want to arrive at knowledge of it, then take the attempt of the thread or of iron, and if the fistula goes according to rectum, and inquire that with it.
But if the fistula is tortuosity, then investigate that with a thread of subtle lead, for lead with the lightness of its body is eased and curved of its tortuosity.
And if the fistula is having moist horrors, it is not to you possible that you signify upon it with thread.
Therefore, cleanse the orifice by its orifices, for the humidity by which you cleanse it should go from the other orifices and run from them.
And then inquire exquisitely, according to what manner to you is it possible that you know if here has the bone or the nerve, and is the concavity of the fistula distant or proximate, or is a fistula to which there are moist orifices and this over all with the sum of your strength, with your interrogation, with which you interrogate the patient, and the invention of the pain you must compress it with your hand over the place, and resemblances of the significations and of the causes accidental to the abscess.

Of the cure of sinews and the quality of clysterization with medicines.
When an abscess occurs in some fleshy members and the space of the abscess is prolonged until it makes a collection of pus, and then it is broken and perforated, and pus is issued from it, and the place remains empty as if it were a vessel, and the skin that is above it as if it were fine cloth, and it has not reached the back corruption, and it has not imprinted on the bone or on the nerve or on the ligament, it is called a sinus, and it is not called a fistula.
But however, if the space is prolonged until the corruption impinges on some member, then it is called a fistula and not a sinus.
And the cure of it is that the skin is incised entirely as if it were turned over, and mostly when it is fine and made like cloth, and comfizas that it does not adhere to the place by its corruption.
But if you hope that the skin adheres and that that corruption has not achieved further consequence, and in the skin has passed through a face, then you cure that with clysters.
And it is that you consider the sinus, and then if it is large, and the brac that you see is of a fetid odor, then you clysterize that with an Egyptian medicine which is of oil and wine and vinegar receiving equal parts, and they are placed in a vessel, and they are boiled over the fire until the medicine becomes thick and reaches the consistency of honey.
And then you take from it what is necessary and dissolve it in water and honey; and clysterize with that the sinus, and strengthen the orifice of it, and leave the medicine in it for the quantity of two hours.
And then extract that with a sponge; and do this for so many days until the sinus is purified and the stench is removed.
And some times it is clysterized with water of ashes, when the medicine is not present to you; and it is that you take the ashes of vitz, and put water on it; and then boil that and clysterize with it until you confess that the sinus is then healed.
And if the patient does not have tolerance on the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ashes, then clysterize that with water and honey and that it be mixed with vinegar, and clysterize that with wine and honey mixed, for by property of honey is that it purifies and washes, and the wine makes the sinus adhere, and especially when in the wine there is superfluity of astringency and dryness.
And as you do this sometimes and you confess that the sinus is already healed, then clysterize that with water that makes flesh grow in it.
And it is that you take of  dyadicon and dissolve it in rose oil and astringent wine; or that you clysterize with it some medicines and other gargles that have the properties which I have already written in the treatise of gargles.
And if the orifice of the sinus is narrow in which the clyster's tube is not received, then you enlarge it with a small iron bit by bit, and place in it a poultice wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it is enlarged.
And similarly if the orifice is wide, then you add the lips of it with suture and leave it in the quantity in which between the clyster its addition.
And if the orifice of him from which the arm comes is elevated to the parts above, then dry that in the lowest place that is in him so that the arm runs below, because when the arm is contracted in the depth of the sinew the flesh is generated in it.
And if it is not possible for you to dry the sinew within the environment of the bone as low as you want, then perforate that which prepares the member with the preparation by which the arm runs lightly as it is to your apparel and that no cause of the arm be retained in it.
But that which is on the orifice of the sinew, the which you remove at every hour so that that which is adjusted in it of the arm may escape. And so that you know if that which runs from it of the arm is much or little, or is digested, or is not digested.
And thus you consider the place of that sinew, if in it the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess in it.
And as your medication is prolonged in this manner, and you see the matter that is thrown on the orifice of the sinew already adheres, or approximates adherence, then the third day you untie it, and when you untie the bandage, then change the cloth for another and renew the enguent.
But if from the sinew a proper space appears virus subtle, then do not despair of its adherence, because the healing of it approaches, because in some men in which slow generation of flesh in their wounds, and of those so in which is done the contrary of it.
And if from the sinew after many days is issued arm indigested, then know that the sinew does not adhere; and if the adherence of the sinew is delayed and is the prolonged cause, then you adjust in drying of the medicines, and if the medicines are humid in their substance and in their virtue, they are dried as in a diaphana enguent, when in it is adjusted superfluity of addition of zegi.

Of the cure of panaritium and ingrown toenails and finger incision and section.
Panaricium is an abscess that arises from beneath the nail of the finger or foot, and it often arises in the other fingers, and as it is prolonged and its cure is less valued, or is an abscess of abscess caut, or is corrupted, and throws out pus while corroding the root of the nail, and often corrupts all of it, and often conveys its corruption to the bone until it is a fetid odor, and the extremity of the finger is made lame, and the color of it is made dusky.
And therefore when you have that with the water that we have said in the division and do not mix your cure, then cover that which you have incised with iron all the superfluity that is remaining of the nail and then cauterize the wound with water, because cauterization is very useful in this.
But if the bone is sound and the nail is healthy, and the additions of the nail voids already encompass the flesh to the sides of the finger, and begin to prick it and let that go, then cover that which you put a fine ray beneath the angle of the nail that pricks the flesh, and impel that up and incise that flesh with ease, and place on that which remains of the flesh of the corrosive burning medicines until it is all removed; and then cure that with enguent until it is healed.
But if the corruption has already entered the bone, then cover that which you have incised the bone and extract it, because no time is healed that which is in it the corrupted bone.
And if you see the corruption and putrefaction going into the wound, then you cut it in one of the nuts according to how the memory of it is pressed, and then take care of it while it is healing.
If the nail is bruised or scratched, and there is pain in that area, then when you first begin to treat the patient, and then dry the nail with a sharp spatula with a transverse section from top to bottom, and be careful that the section does not reach into the flesh that remains under the nail, because you will cause the patient to have severe pain, and it will cause the birth of superfluous flesh in the area; and then take care of that area with water that soothes the pain.
But this adjusted flesh, which is born in the hands of some men, is very fleshy, and it is very fleshy in the bones, or very fleshy in the nail.
And some of them are born at the root of the joint, or the birth of them in some nuts of the fingers. But the one that is born in some nuts of the finger does not hurt, and the one that is born in the joints is very painful.
And of those that are born fleshy, the section is lighter, and that you cut with a spatula flat.
But the one that is born at the root of the joint, the cure is difficult; and therefore guard yourself from the abscess of it.
But in the one that is born in the finger, when you begin, cut the flesh of it with a round incision into the bone, and then saw it with one of those saws suitable for water, and then take care of it while it is healing.
But consolidation, which happens to the fingers between their movements or by birth of the man who is born with it, or by consolidation of plague or by burning of fire, or by similar things, therefore, when you cut that consolidation while the fingers return to their natural form.
And then place between their cloths of the infused in olive oil so that they are not consolidated lightly, and separate between them, or place between them a thin sheet of lead while it is consolidated as it should be.
And similarly if consolidation happens in some fingers with the palm, then you cut that consolidation according to how it is prepared and convenient to the figure of the limb.
Of incisions of vices, they are varicose.
Vices are varicose, and they are thick veins full of melancholic superfluities that come in motion in the limbs of the body, and the greater coming of them in the legs, and most in the legs of the travelers and the laborers and the carriers.
Therefore, it is necessary that you administer purgatives of the body of black bile some times with forceful expulsion, and then bleed the patient from the basilica vein.
But the cure of them with iron is according to two manners: one is that it be incised and that the black blood be thrown out, and the other manner is that the vein be elevated and all of it be extracted.
The incision of it is according to this manner: at the beginning, embroil the leg with warm water so that the thick blood be resolved, which is feculent of the leg, and then strengthen the leg of the patient to the most sovereign part of the thigh, and then to the part below the knee with a bandage, and then cut the vein in one place, or in two, or in three with a wide section, and then elevate the black blood with your hand from the part below the leg and up, and down, until the amount of blood that you want and that you see is enough, and which will take the virtue of the malady.
And then tie that, and command him that he abstain from the foods that engender black bile.
And repeat the cure by phlebotomy when the veins are full and that night to the patient.
But the elevation of them is according to this manner: you that raise the leg of the patient, if in it there are motions, and then put it in a bath and embroil the leg of it with warm water until it becomes reddish and the veins are exuberant; or that it be exercised by strong exercise, if the bath is not present, until the limb is warmed.
And then cut the vein in the right of it, by incision in the long or in the back of it of the knee, or in the lowest part of it of the ankle.
And then open the vein with pincers and scrape the vein from all parts until it appears to the touch, and it is of the appearance of it that you see that black color declining.
And therefore when you evacuate from the vein, you see that white which is cord.
And then you put below that the ray until it is elevated and it is thrown from the vein, and suspend that with a lion's orp onion.
And then cut another incision near that one for three fingers, and then scrape the vein from the part below the vein until it appears.
And then elevate that and cut that in the back incision of the ankle, and then extract that and elevate it until it is gone through the second incision, and then extract that from the incision that is above that.
And do this until you extract that from the incision that is most sovereign or most high of all the incisions, until all is gone; and then cut that.
And if it does not obey to you to extract and elevate, then introduce a needle with a strong double thread and tie that and extract it, or introduce behind it the ray and revolve your hand to all parts until it is ejected. And guard yourself that it not be incised; for if it is broken, it is made difficult to elevate that part and it has come upon the patient by that harm.
And when that whole area is moved, then place on the location of the plague wool submerged in wine and oil, both rubbed and unrubbed, and cure that until it is healed.
And if the gut is contracted having tortuosity in its wrapping at the parts, and it is not according to rectitude according to what we have said, then cover that which you do on all parts of its tortuosity and at the locations of its wrapping, and then suspend that with hooks until you elevate that whole thing.
And guard yourself that your section does not cut the vein and that you do not harm that, for it is difficult for you to elevate that; and serve your prudence in that.

It is not to it acute as with the hooks nor is it of sharp extremity so that it does not harm the vein; and it is of gross flexibility leon, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein by its subtlety; it has in it superfluous thickness as we have said.

On the section for the ailment of nafir.
This ailment is called nafir in our land, and it is pain that comes in certain limbs, and then it is changed from limb to limb.
And I have already seen that, as I will tell you. I was called to a sick woman in a village, and I uncovered her arm and saw a small inflation in the vein of the arm, and because it was warm for an hour, I saw that inflation go as if a worm was pushing it, but more lightly than being felt, as if it were living silver when it runs from place to place.
And then it moved to the pain of that place and it felt in the muscle, and then it stayed there for an hour.
And then it moved to the other body until it reached the other arm.
And then I recommended to her that she should turn herself over her whole body as I had seen; and I was too amazed by the mutation of it and the speed of limb to limb. And I had already seen this before in my own eyes in that manner, however, I have seen many who suffer pain being changed from limb to limb. But I did not see this in the eyes as in the woman.
And I did not think that this was anything but because the woman was old, on whose dry body and exposed veins, and in this appearance, that mutability was felt.
And it is necessary that it does not appear according to this retro-cure in those who are delicate and with moist bodies of well-covered veins.
And as you want the cure of it, and the patient feels that pain, then it is not to you apparent in the eye as we have said, then you tighten over it and leave it lightly and press over it until that mutability is constricted, and cauterize the location.
But if you do not see it with your eyes, then you cure it with the shaking of the body and with that which you expel the mutability, and charm it with pills foul-smelling and with pills of serpent and the like.
On the extraction of arrows.
Arrows are diversified according to the species, and according to the places of the body in which they strike, because their diversity is that of those that have large tips, and small, and concave, and blunt, they are solid; and of those that have three angles, and of those that have tongues; and of those that have shafts.
And of the signs of the neck is when it strikes in it an arrow, and it pierces the bone, and it is issued from the cyph of which is above the brain, because it happens through it with a vehement soda, and scotoma, and vertigo, and roaring in the eyes, and inflammation and roaring of the tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding and vomiting of bile, and very much the word is cut off and the voice is destroyed, and it is issued from the place of the wound a white moisture similar to dust, and tears from it resembling the moisture of the flesh.
And therefore if these signs appear to you, then you abstain from the cure and the extraction of the arrow, if it is not outside.
But the signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart, are that it is near the left nipple, and feels with that which it is fixed in a hard cause, and it is not a hollow cause; and very much the movement of the arrow is similar to the movement of the pulse, and the running of the wound black blood, and seizes that coldness of the extremities, and sweat chills, and syncope; and therefore you know that death descends all over it.
And the signs when the arrow has wounded the lung are so much blood sputtered from the wound, and the vessels that are near the neck are inflamed, and the color of the patient is changed, and he expires great spirit, and demands the suction of cold air.
And if it strikes the arrow in the ligament which is in the foot, and the pain then is near the small ribs, and it is made great pain with vehement pain and sigh, and not bad all the members of the muscles.
And if it strikes the arrow in the stomach, then very much tears from the wound food somewhat indigested.
And if it strikes the arrow in the belly, and it is fixed in it, tears from the wound some of the fabric, or the intestine, which is disrupted, and there is no hope in the cure of it the extraction of the arrow.
And if the arrow enters the bladder, and urine is expelled outside, and something processes from it to the outside parts, and there is a lot of pain on the patient, then you know that it is mortal.
But the other members like the face, the neck, the throat, the shoulders and the helpers, the vertebrae of the back, the clavicle, the hip, the leg and their likeness of the members, are saved according to the major dispositions when the arrow does not hit a vein or artery and is not a poisonous arrow.
And I recount this to you that I have seen of the nature of these arrows, so that you may signify it for your cure.
The cause is, that in a man a shot arrow in the lacrimal of his eye in the root of the nose, and you extracted it from the other part, leaving the gray of the eyelid of him, and it is healed, and it did not cause any harm in the eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Jew who was shot in his eye, leaving the eyelid, and the arrow was already hidden and could not be obtained from it except for a small extremity with which it adhered to its shaft, and it was a large arrow of the sharp arrows of the Turks, with a lion's iron in which there were no eyelids.
And the Jew healed, and it did not cause any harm to his eye.
And I extracted another arrow from a Christian man which was shot in the throat, and it was an Arabic arrow, and it is the one that has eyelids; and therefore I incised it between two guides, and it was already submerged in his throat; and then I subdued it with that, and then I extracted it, and the Christian healed.
And I extracted another arrow from a man who was shot in his belly, and I thought he would die from it; and therefore, because forty days had passed and nothing had changed about him from his dispositions, I incised it on the arrow and engineered it, and he healed, and it did not cause him any harm.
And I saw another man in whom an arrow was shot in his back, and the wound was consolidated on him, and because it was about seven years, he pulled the arrow out from the root of the groin.
And I saw a woman to whom an arrow was shot in her belly, and the wound was consolidated from within her, and it was not changed in her dispositions in any way, and the woman did not suffer any harm in any of her natural operations.
And I saw another man to whom an arrow was shot in his face and the wound was consolidated, and he broke the arrow, not feeling much pain, and many similar things happened to this one.
And I extracted the arrow from the man of the king's princes who was shot in the middle of his nose and it had already declined to the right a little, and the whole arrow was hidden.
And I was called to his cure after the shooting of the arrow entered three days.
And then I examined the wound of the arrow very carefully; and then I inquired about it with a subtle touch, and I did not feel it; but I felt a prick below the right eyelid, and therefore I suspected that that prick was because of the extremity of the arrow.
And I plastered the place with a plaster in which there is attractive and digestive virtue, confessing to myself that the place would be apostematized so that it would appear to me the location of the arrow, so that it would dry out on it.
And it did not cause any harm to the location significant that the arrow had reached that place; and I continued with the plaster on it for many days and it did not cause any harm; and the wound was consolidated meanwhile, and he broke the ailment of the extraction of him for a space of many days until one day he felt the arrow inside his nose and recounted this to me.
And then I placed on the wound medicine acute corrosive for many days until it opened, and with the touch I felt it, and I examined that, and extracted the extremity of the arrow subtly, which adhered to the shaft.
And then I adjusted it in the appearance of the wound with that medicine acute until it appeared to me visibly the extremity of the arrow, and passed to me time with that for the space of time within four months.

Of phlebotomy of the veins.
The veins of phlebotomy of which it is customary to phlebotomize about .xxx., of which there are in the head .xvi., There are two pulsatile veins which are near the ears, called alhasisain; two herbs that are in the two temples appear; and two veins that are in two lacrimals of two bones that are called aspicientz; and the prepared vein in the middle place of the forehead, and the vein that is in the extremity of the nose; and two guidegi that are in the neck; and two veins that are in the upper lip; and two veins that are in the lower lip; and— these are the veins that are called algelic—; and there are two veins that are below the tongue. But the veins that are phlebotomized in the arms are .v.; because of those is one cephalic, and it is the wild latz; and the people call “the vein of the head”, and blunt, and it is a medium vein, and it is composed of a branch of the basilica, and another branch of the cephalic; and that one the people call “vein of the whole body”, and basilica is the vein that is placed in the domestic latz, and it is called “citillar”, and they call that one the vulgarians “vein of the belly”; and funis of the arm, and it is placed above the focil, and it is that one in which it is phlebotomized, and it is that one that appears on the poutz by manifest appearance; and salvatella, and it is the vein that is between the little said auricular and the smallest said, and there are two ramps in it.
And in the foot and the leg there are three veins; one of those is that which is below the curvature of the denolh of the wild latz; and the second is sophena, and its place is below the leg of the domestic latz; and the sciatic vein, and its place is below the leg of the wild latz; and in the leg there are other veins similar to those.
The benefit of the veins that are near the ears is for ancient catarrh and emigration and sahafati and ancient bad ulcers of the head.
And the quality of bleeding those is according to what I recommend to you: it is that it be scraped the head of the patient, and it be rubbed the head of the patient in the occiput in the place of both the veins with a wide cloth with good friction; then tighten the patient's neck with a bandage until the two appear and the places of their being near the ears in two depressed places of the head; and you want that one with your finger, and if you feel the pulse of those with your finger, here send a attempt.
Then you take the sharp lance, and it is that one that is incident, and then you introduce that below the vein in the codena until the phlebotomy comes to the bone. And then you raise your hand with the vein and the codena to the upper parts and you cut the vein with an incident incision. And let the length of the incision be the quantity of two fingers adjusted or around that; and do as much of the blood as you want.
And then tighten with poultices and leave it until it is healed.
And already it has been preceded at the beginning of the book the incision of those and their cauterization.
But of the two arterial veins that are in the temples the benefit of phlebotomy is for ancient emigration and bad and obstinate ophthalmia and acute superfluity effused to the bones.

And then you elevate the codena above the vein to the upper parts with your finger indicating, and introduce the phlebotomy incident below, and elevate the vein upwards; and cut that as you have done in the other two veins; and make the blood run according to the quantity of your need.
And then untie the constriction of the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, and then put on that coat and poultices and tighten that above with strong constriction, and leave it until it is healed.
And already is preceded the remembrance of them, and of those the incision, and the traction at the beginning of the book.

The first of these is that you should know that phlebotomy is not administered except in the preservation of health and for the hope of it and the prevention of diseases, and that it should be performed on one of the veins that are in the arm, namely: cephalic, basilic and median cubital; and that it should be performed at the beginning of spring, fasting in spring and autumn, and in winter near the meal, when there appear signs of repletion.
And it should be performed phlebotomy on the third day or at the first hour that three hours have passed from the day.
But phlebotomy that is administered, more when it provokes convenience and necessity to it, either at night or day, at any hour and at any time.
And you should know that a child should not be phlebotomized before they have fourteen years, and a woman who is pregnant should not be phlebotomized except from the fourth month until the seventh, and the elderly should not be phlebotomized those who have already passed sixty years.
And since someone wants to be phlebotomized in any way, you should make them cleanse their bowels before the phlebotomy with a laxative enema, if in those there is much retained feces, so that the veins do not throw the superfluities into the phlebotomy of the bowels, which are cleansed, and that they do not harm the principal members.
And they should not be phlebotomized patients nauseous, acutely sick, or drunk, nor evading illness or drunkenness until it is removed from them, nor those with dropsy, but rather that phlebotomy should be feared near colic, vomiting, and abdominal pain, and near multiplication of coitus and labor and exercise of fasting or vigils and of any cause that dissolves the virtue, whether corporal or animal.
And before it, consider in the subtility of humors, if the blood is thick, with foods and drinks, and with medicines if it is possible to it.
And before it, introduce into a bath if no cause prohibits it, or exercise by any exercise so that the blood is made more subtle.
And pause the phlebotomy of it in the afternoon of the day, that is around the hour of terce, as we have said.
And perforsa te that the patient's foot be guarded on that day from all evil accidents, both animal, such as anxiety, anger, fear, and all corporal accidents, such as labor and superfluous pain and coitus and similar things to them.
And to his bed, make it present the causes in the use of which custom of men with aromaticity and odor and with balsams and similar things according to the quantity of possibility.

And let the stricture be temperate, for the stricture when it is not equal, or the stricture is with superfluity, then prohibit the flow of blood; or it is with softening, and then prohibit the body of blood from rising.
And before the stricture, you should know that the one who is to be phlebotomized rub their hands together while the veins are inflamed, and are declared to the feeling.
And before the phlebotomist, anoint their phlebotomy with a little bit of olive oil properly; and place their left hand index over that vein, below the location of which the phlebotomy is desired, so that the vein may be a little pushed out, and the percussion be seated, for of the veins is the one that is throbbing as the heart flees, and of those is the one that is full of vitality, and when you place the phlebotomy upon it, it is contracted, and the phlebotomist is revealed; and the phlebotomy does not pierce the vein, and if it does, then that is constricted.
And therefore, for this, the phlebotomist should be halted and be solicited in all these causes.
And after the phlebotomy, but if the vein is pierced in one go, then it is good; and if not, then repeat it another time below that location a little, or upon it with a little pressure, if the location is not inflamed.
And if the location is inflamed, or the patient becomes frightened, then you leave it for a day or two, and do not stretch the ligament, because forcefully pulling it will draw the abscess outwards, nor enter into a bath.
And after, repeat the phlebotomy if necessary.
And if the incision is small and the blood flows subtly, and you fear that it will not be the quantity of blood you desire, then you repeat the phlebotomy in that tract according to rectitude and adjust in the incision a little, and do it with pressure before the location is inflamed, because the location is inflamed in many men of little incision.
But if sometimes that is already inflamed, then do not repeat upon it, because it excuses you no cause; and place upon it some part of the incision of olive oil, because it alleviates the body of the blood. And it is better in this place than oil and other oils.
And similarly, administer a wound of oil in every phlebotomy with which phlebotomize the veins that are forbidden by the body of blood, and do this tyriaca alfadoc and sagzenea when it is placed on the spot, for the blood is subtiliated and is revolted when it is thick.

Of suction and the qualities of using them.
Suctions are of horns, or of wood, or of leather.
And suction is done in two ways: one of them is with scarification and extraction of blood, and the other is suction without scarification.
And this suction that is without scarification is in two ways, whether it is with fire or without fire.
And to the suctions that are administered with scarification and extraction of blood there are fourteen places of the body, of which one in which suctions are placed is the occiput, and it is the back part of the head; and the middle place of the two parts of the neck together; and suctions of the chin below the jawbone below the mouth; and suctions of the two scapulas; and suctions of the hypochondria, and it is above the end of the rib cage; and suctions of the two armpits; and suctions of the two groins.
And suction does not extract blood from the small veins scattered in the flesh, and therefore it does not catch the virtue through them, as it is caught by phlebotomy; nor should it be that suction be done with fire or without fire in any disease caused by repletion until the whole body is evacuated.
But if necessity provokes suction for illness or for continuous, administer it at all hours at the beginning of the month and at the end of it, and in the middle of it and at any time.
And therefore when sometimes in any cause of those, and properly if it is in the third or middle of the month, then command suction to be done more than it has passed from the day two or three hours.
And the benefit of suction of the neck is that when that confers gravity to the head and to that which is effused to the eyes; but it is necessary that that be near evacuation of the whole body.
And this suction is in the place of phlebotomy of the cephalic.
And it is not light that use of it that one who is of cold complexion, or in whom is catarr, for it gives to that great harm.
And for that reason it is not necessary that use of that the old, and in the heads of which are cold diseases.
But to that one who over that is continuing over it is done oblivion; and for that reason it is necessary that you command the suction-maker to pause his hand a little with the suction to the parts below, fearing the generation of oblivion.
But suction of the elbow is in the place of phlebotomy of the vena fusca and of the basilica: and for that reason confers to asthma, and to the constriction of the ale and to the scissura of the sturment of ale, and to cough, and to repletion.
And it is necessary that the elbow suction be peeled a little, for if it is paused below, it engenders weakness in the body and in the stomach.
And the suction of alhagdahan confers to the pains accident in the head and to ophthalmia, and migraine, and prefoco, and pains in the roots of the teeth; and it is in the place of phlebotomy of the basilica.
And it is necessary that you command the suction-maker that he not press his hand with scarification for that it does not pierce the artery and happens flux of blood.
And suction below the chin confers to alcohol in the mouth, and to corruption of the gums, and appearances to those of the diseases that are in the mouth, and stand in the place of phlebotomy of aliheric that is in the two lips.
But the suction that is done upon the two scapulas confers to caphatan, which is made by repletion of heat.
And the suction of the two parts of the armpits confers benefit of phlebotomy of three veins, so it is of the basilica, fusca and cephalic, for that one attracts the blood of all those veins more slender that are in the flesh, and those veins slender of the other veins more gross within that it reaches the attraction to the three veins.
And command the suction-maker that too much he does not proceed in scarification, for the place is denuded of flesh, and below it are nerves and arteries.
And it is a suction with which is suctioned upon the buttocks and confers to the hemorrhoids of the anus and to the ulcers below.
And command the ventor to be a strong ventor, and that it be of iron, for the place needs a strong section; and very fine and subtle ventor be scarified with a scarification.
But the ventors of the legs are less so by minutia, because they draw the blood of the whole body, and compare to old pains of the lungs and the womb, and the bladder; and they provoke the menses, and compare to both and a little; and they are in the place of fleubotomia of two sophenas, and alahorcoben, and of two cavilhas.
But they weaken the whole body and cause syncope in many men.
And of the ventors, the alahorcoben is proper to the alahorcoben of the two legs.
And the quality of the position of the ventors is that you pause the ventor at the beginning, and suck it gently, and do not prolong the position of the ventors, but pause them lightly, and move them gently, and that the humors come to the place by equal advancement. And do not cease to iterate this and continue until you see the place already reddened and inflated and that the color of the blood appears.
And then you scarify and iterate the suction little by little, and then consider in the disposition of the body.
Because that man who has tender flesh of rare pores, you should scarify him once and no more, for that the place not be ulcerated.
And command the ventor to amplify the scarification and proceed a little, and temper the suction with facility.
And if in the blood is thickness, then you should scarify twice, because in the first scarification is opened the way of subtilization to the blood and the liquidity of it. But in the second to the scrutiny acquired of the extraction of the thick blood.
And if the blood is very feculent, then let the third scarification be made so that it may obtain the last.
And finally, when we want to extract the blood little by little or a little, it suffices us one scarification.
And if we want the extraction of much blood, we scarify with much scarification; and if we knew that the blood is thick, then we should scarify by pre-scarification.
And the term of scarification in which is the depth of the code only.
And if that one whose code is thick, hard, dark, and whose pores are strait, then the places of the ventors should be anointed more gently, more open, more resolved; if it is in summer, as is olive of aloe or olive of violet, or olive of double amygdalas, or olive of quince; and if it is in winter, then olive of narcissus, or olive of lily, or olive of chamomile, or of saffron, and to those resemblances.
And if the superfluity is thick, sticky, then the olive should be of amaranth, or olive of balsamita, or olive of aloe, or olive of aneth, and to their resemblances.
But if the ventor is of wide pores of tender flesh, then it should be prohibited from oil, and it should have the places of the ventors near them be washed with water or with cold water of solanum, or with quince water, or with water of bordolaguas, and resemblances to those.
And that one whose blood is of much humidity, wash his ventors with strong wine, or with water of myrtle and sumac and resemblances to those.
And of that one whose superfluities are thick, wash his ventors with old wine, or with water of sansuc, which is marjoram, or of decoction of aneth, or of chamomile, and to their resemblances.
And the ventor should be guarded before bathing; bathing should be administered near the bath for an hour or two, and should sleep near the ventor.
What is what should be done to regulate the ventor before phlebotomy.
You should consider at the beginning: then if the ventor or the one who is to be phlebotomized is choleric and has a sharp and inflamed blood, then they should be pre-treated with cold causes, such as vinegar, endive with strong wine and lettuce, and secanabin, and julep, and to their resemblances.
And pause their foods as much as possible, and birds' meats, and foods seasoned with acids, and to their resemblances.
And of that one whose complexion is cold, they should be pre-treated with drinking syrup of almiva, or syrup of alsecanabin of seeds, and sumac, and wine very fragrant between old and new; and that he should be commanded to use little drinking and eating, and pause the foods of his little and canary and sparrow and small birds and dove.
And that on the day of ventorization and phlebotomy, the drink should be greater than the food.
And that some men should be given to drink in some hours tyriaca alpharac, or medicines of musk, so it is muscata, or alcelita before the ventorization or before phlebotomy or near, so that the main limbs be comforted and the blood be subtilized; and that they should not take that scalfatz.
But the cuts that are made as incisions should be cuts that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen and gout, and on the navel, in the places of the joints, and the hip, because these members do not suffer incisions on themselves.
And it is not desired for those, but rather the attraction of blood from the limb, just as we place a suction cup on the nipple in the illness of blood flow from the nose; and we use it so that the cold suction may dissolve from the limb, just as we place it on the belly and the navel; because it thins the limb and heats it and removes the pain by dissolving the suction.
And it is already placed on the boils when they occur in their opening or pimple, because by virtue of the strong attraction they open the pimple and eradicate the pimple from its place.
And similarly it does when it is placed on the liver and spleen with suction in those enclosed places.
And these incisions are administered empty with suction alone; and some times they are administered with fire.
And some times they are administered full of tepid water in the illnesses of the spleen.
And this is so that the incision may be filled and be larger, so it is water poured alone or water in which herbs are boiled for the appropriate purpose.
Method of a suction cup administered with fire: its orifice size is two fingers, according to how we have formed it; and the amount of the resin is the majority of a palm; and it is in the middle of it, in the place that is in the circuit, the majority of it, the trough is small according to the amount that enters it a needle.
Let it be made of a smooth, hard, and thick, lemon, with large edges, lion, equal, and smooth so that it does not damage the limb of its position on it.
And in the middle of it, a transverse rod of copper or iron, on which a candle is placed with the fire.
And already this suction cup is larger than the one we have described; and the small one less according to the illnesses and the state of the one who uses it.
And the suction cups of the infants and the weak are other than the suction cups of the young and of robust bodies.
And the quality of placing this suction cup with fire on the limb is that it extends the fire with wood decently in front of a small candle of wax, and place it on the middle of the transverse rod in the middle place of the suction cup, so that the fire is ignited around the part so that it does not burn the body of the patient.
And then it is placed on the limb of the patient, and the finger is on the trough that we have said, and when we have the suction cups and do not indicate that we show the finger and that it escapes the vapor on that trough, then the suction cup is dissolved instantly.
And properly ignite the fire according to its manner, and repeat that if you indicate it.
But in a suction cup that is administered in the illness of pleurisy, with water, in which there is no transverse rod nor trough, and it is not administered unless it is filled with water, and it is placed on the limb alone.
And this is the form of it: And this suction cup, the more it is large, the better, because it can receive a large quantity of water.
