And it is reduced easily in another manner: and it is that a long staff be placed on the ground, the head of which is rounded in shape, as if a mortar, that it be neither thick nor thin, and then placed below the patient; because on the head of the staff, linen cloths are placed, and the patient stands according to the length of the staff, and then the hand of him is extended to the parts below the other side; and the body of him is extended from the other side with strength, for the joint returns to its place with speed.
And if the reduction of it is difficult for all the causes that we have said, then use this cure: and it is that you take a staff the length of which is in the length of two arms, and the width of it is of four fingers, and the thickness of it is lessened in the middle of the thigh according to this form:
And on the rounded head, there are placed linen cloths so that the staff does not hurt the patient.
And then it is placed below the thigh of the patient, and the hand or arm is extended over the staff into the parts below, and the staff is tied over the assistant and the arm and the extremity of the hand.
Then the arm is placed on a step of a ladder according to the width, and the hand is extended to the parts below, and the other body is suspended from the other side, for the joint enters instantly.
And as the entry of it is completed in whichever manner that is possible to you, then know that you should place below the thigh a bandage of linen of equal quantity; and then place a plaster prepared of powder of meal mixed with eggs and albumen of egg over the whole muscle, so that it is rolled upwards, and then a strength below the thigh with decent constriction; and the ligament is rolled over the plaster, and the hand of him is attached to the neck of him, and it is left, and the hand of him is not moved for seven days.
And that the patient's food be kept small, until the limb is comforted, for it is lighter for its healing.
And then when the food is given greater near the fifth or sixth, and movement is exercised; and therefore if it is stopped and not softened, then it is already healed.
But if the joint is dislocated many times by humidity that happens to it or for another cause, then it is necessary that in that one cautery is administered with three points, according to what is said before in the chapter of cautery.
And if all this is done and after seven days the ligament is loosened and the joint is not fixed, and the plaster and the constriction are reduced over it several times, and it is not fixed and it catz and cannot elevate that arm to the upper parts, then know that the nerves of it, which are at the head of the muscle, are already cut or extended or softened, and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Of the dislocation of that one which is made of the foot and the heel or the parts behind, the reduction is made with impulse and extension with the hands, until it returns.
And let the other constriction be administered in that one, and care for that one until it is healed.
And if it happens that during healing gravity falls on the limb and slowness in its movement, then the patient uses baths many times until that gravity is relieved and returns to its nature first.
Chapter .xxvii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the hip.
Know that the hip joint is dislocated with difficulty and seemingly returns with difficulty; and that is dislocated to all parts, and more to the front part than to the back part, and the dislocation of it is not easy to be known because it is hidden from the sight or from the touch according to what figure it is dislocated, and when you adjust the dislocated hip with the hand, this is declared to you manifestly, because the joint is concave and cannot bend the arm, nor touch with that one its muscle.
And that you set the hips, and reduce the dislocation as soon as possible before an abscess comes to it, for if it comes to it an abscess, the reduction is difficult, and it is not healed of all; and more so when it is in the back parts, because it is worse of all the other kinds of dislocations, and of greater pain, and many times they leave to it death.
And the restoration of it, when that one is possible to reduce, is that the hand of it be extended with two hands, and the arm of it be expanded, and the hands of the doctor be over the hip and under it, and he pushes the joint with the knuckles of his hands together, or with the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
But if the dislocation is in the front parts, then it returns as if bending the hand with its hand, until it strikes the hip with the root of its palm.
And if the dislocation does not obey the reduction, then administer vehement extension and strong force.
And it is that two ministers extend the arm, and hold that raising of the ministers so that it is not remounted from the extension.
And then be revolved the arm completely, because it is enveloped cloth folded long over the hand of it, or ligament.
And when the doctor touches the joint with his hand, anoint that one with some oil so that this is those causes which help in the lubrication of the joint with facility; and then pushes the joint with impulse vehement until it returns.
And after the reduction of it, it is necessary that it be laid upon that plaster in which there is sticking and application with album of egg, and be extended with a descending constriction, and the arm be suspended from the neck, and be left for some days.
And after it is loosened; and therefore if the joint is formed in its place, then you loosen the ligament of it and leave it.
And if sometimes the joint does not become stronger, then you reiterate the plaster and the ligament, and leave it for some days until it is extended; and after loosen it.
But if it happens to it gravity after the reduction of the joint, and the disposition of it is in movement, then administer moisture in baths and subtle friction, and compression, until it is relieved; or place over the joint a poultice of greasy matter; and then be bound, and leave it over the bones both day and night. And after you remove that, and put that one in a bath; and when it is dry, then you rub the joint with temperate friction, and then reiterate over that poultice, so is a poultice of greasy matter, once, and the second, and the third. Corruption has already arrived upon the tooth inside the mouth, while it is still soft.
And if you want, place over that a piece of cowhide wet and scalded with butter and strengthened over that; and do this some times, because that one is wet and reduces to its disposition.
Chapter .xxviii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the malassen, so is of the joint that is between the arm and the hand.
Malassen of the hand some times is dislocated, and the reduction of the dislocation of it is lighter, and the contrary is of the other joints, but however, it is necessary that it be velocity in the reduction of it in the hour in which it is dislocated, before the place is apostematized or that something happens to it abscess.
And the reduction of the dislocation of him is that you place the joint of the patient's hand on a table and the assistant extends the hand of that one, and the doctor places his hand or his palm on the prominence of the joint, and pushes it in while it returns to its place.
But however, it should be considered if the palm is already placed on the belly of the hand, then the patient places the back of his hand on a table,  and the extension and reduction; and if the dislocation is precedent, then the back of the hand, then the position of the hand of that one intrinsically on the table, so that the hand of the doctor lies on that prominence of the joint.
And therefore if it returns at once, it is good; and if not, then strengthen that with a poultice,  yielding the abscess and leaving it; and do not repeat this, because if not, do not suffer nor can you over the reduction of it more than days pass.
But however, the joint remains according to its tortuosity; and do not notice to the patient any cause, except that the hand is softened and cannot strengthen any cause; then you know that the nerves are broken or twisted, and then there is no remedy in it except that it be strengthened with a cautery near the place of it and very strongly confer any cause.
Therefore, as the malasse is returned, then place on it the poultice which have recomposed, and let it be left and strengthened for 5 days; and then it should be removed and let it be left and the hand of it be exercised.
But if the movement of it is stayed and there is any weight on it, then gently that with water cauda and with friction several times, until it is relieved.
Chapter .xxix.
Of the cure of dislocations of the said.
Sometimes the fingers are dislocated in every part.
And when a finger is dislocated of those at the back of the palm or on the belly of it, then stretch the finger and push the dislocation of it with your fingers, until it returns.
And then support the head of the finger, and suspend that part to which it is dislocated, and leave it for two days.
And then suspend that and extend that until straight it is healed in that its day.
And when it will be night, tie that according to that narration, and do not cease to untie that in the day and exercise with movement, and tie that in the night; and do this for some days until it is straight.
And do seeming with this, if it is dislocated on the belly of the hand, and tie that to that part and do with this your first operation, until it is healed.
And similarly do with this when it is dislocated to the other parts.
Chapter .xxx.
Of the cure of dislocations of the vertebrae of the back.
When an accident happens to any of the vertebrae of the back or of the neck, a complicated dislocation, and the movable vertebrae are removed from their places, then in that there is no cure, because death takes hold of the patient.
And a sign of this is that the digestion of the patient is outside his will, and he cannot retain that; and many times are softened some limbs of him or two legs of him or two arms of him, or one of those; or a vertebra is removed from its place, because many times it is removed and many times is made the removal of those to four parts.
Therefore that is already removed to the parts behind and is called gelbozit.
But the cure of it is that then you consider if the gelbozit accident of puerility, because then in that there is no cure nor of that there is no healing of all.
But in that which comes by accident or by percussion or seeming to those, already said the Ancients the ways of cure with sermon prolixs, of which the most returns with prophecy; but I have already and abbreviated of that of which the few excuses of the trop of it, for the my better proximity to the better understanding exposition, with which I have this exposed and formed ex instrument divers of that with which I show this and expose that.
And of those there is no cure except that which accidents in the back properly with this that I have recomposed.
And it is that the patient be extended on his face over a pug even proper of wall, and be extended below him instrument molh so that not be lifted the feet of him.
And then a straight stick be placed, fixed in the earth at the extremity of the pug around the head of it, and another stick in the aviro the feet of it at the other extremity of the pug.
And the assistant holds the stick, and it not be fixed in fossa; and another assistant holds the other according to that form.
And then envelop over the head of the patient and below the titilllic liamen leon firm; and extend the extremity of the liamen to the stick which is of the head of it, and tie that in it; and then strengthen the other liament over the hips of it the denols of it, and of the legs of it; and then adjust all the liamentz and tie those in the other stick which is of the feet of it.
And then the minister, having casqued, extends the ligament to the part of the shaft, and do not be removed the two shafts and ligaments of their places in which they are placed, but however do not be stopped as we have said.
And the physician places his palms on the spine with strength while it returns, or that which places upon that a table, and then that adjusts upon the table his feet while it returns.
But if it does not return in this way, then take a table of which the width or length be in a ratio of three braccia, and carve in the wall of which we have said that it is near the patient a place in which enters the extremity of the table. And then place the majority of the table upon the spine, and the physician places his feet upon the other extremity, and strengthens well until the spine be contracted and that it returns to its place.
And if you wish, open with a turn the one that is revolved with the hand; and it is that you fix on the ground the head of the patient in the rear of the pug two shafts, the length of which be of one braccio, and in the rear of the pug also two shafts; and be the length that is between each shaft a palm, and already is made in each shaft a trough in which runs the turn, and each one be firmly fixed on the ground so that it not be moved.
And be also a shaft rounded in which is the turn, and be revolved in the two troughs of the two shafts.
And in the extremity of it is a trough in which is formed the shaft, the length of which is a palm with that which is revolved; and in the two other shafts is similar to that.
And then strengthen the ligaments that you have straightened in the feet of the patient in the trough which is in the rear of the head of it, and the ligaments that you have straightened in the thighs of it in the turn which is in the rear of the feet of it.
And then place each turn and stay a minister that twists the turn with his hand, and the physician engualhe the spine according to what we have said.
And as soon as the spine is returned, and the place is aligned, then cover that you place a plaster exsiccative with album of how, and then cotton; and then place upon the plaster a table of which the width be of three digits or around those, and the length of it be the quantity that prengues the place of the yellowness, and upon the part of the spine it be.
And then tie it with the ligament which we have said, and use the patient of subtle nourishment until it be healed.
And if there remain any imminence in the place at the end of the healing, then cover that medicines be administered that soften and cleanse with administration of the table for long time, which we have recommended; and already is administered in that place a lamina of lead.
And some times accidents imminence in the rear of the spines of the two, and it is cured by that dislocation; and it is that bone which already imineys for that you cover that it be made prosompcio to it with this medicine, because very strong it will make you to happen death.
Chapter .xxxI.
Of the cure of a dislocated hip.
Know that the joint of the hip and the joint of the muscle should not be dislocated only, and accidents do not happen to those that happen to the other joints of small movement and concavity.
And the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four manners, because it is dislocated to the parts in front, or to the parts outside, or to the parts behind, or to the parts in front.
And mostly it is dislocated to the parts in front, and few to the parts behind or to the parts in front.
And the sign of the dislocation of it to the parts in front is that, when you adjust the leg of the healthy patient with the patient, it is longer and the tendon is more prominent than of the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their leg in front of the knee, and it is the place that if the knee is inflamed with cautery, so that the head of the thigh has already arrived here.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation is to the parts outside, is that the accidents of it are contrary to this accident.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation to the parts in front is that it expands its leg according to its complement, but however it does not bend that which is pain in the tendon, and if it persists to go and cannot over that to the parts in front; and the urine of it is retained and the groin of it is inflamed, and of the ambulation of it over the heel.
And the sign of that one which happens dislocation to the parts behind is that it does not expand the tendon, nor can it bend that which bends the groin, and the leg of it is shorter than the other, and the groin is softened, and the head of the thigh is in that place.
But the reduction of the species of this dislocation is that you consider, then, if the dislocation is old and ancient, that it is already fixed with that one, then you administer reduction of it and it remains according to its disposition, then it is not in that cure of all; and therefore you cover that in that one be made prosompcio.
But in the case of which the dislocation is recent, and is one of the four species of dislocation, then take hold of that which you want to return the joint and extend it to the inside and outside parts, and move it to the right and left, for it will return very quickly and does not need other care.
But if it does not return in this manner, then take hold of that which you prepare, and extend the leg of the patient from the back part, or by his hands, or by a bandage which is tied above the knee; and another minister extend the hand of that one from below so that he puts his hands behind the knees of him; and then tighten with a bandage on the root of the groin, and hold another minister the extremity of the bandage.
And the extension of him or from the inside part to the angle of the collarbone, or from the back part to the part of the spine.
And the extension of all those at once while the patient is elevated with his body from the ground and remains hanging.
And this species of extension is special common to all four.
And therefore if the dislocation returns with what we have said, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to all species that we will say of the proper cure.
In the reduction of him proper, when he is dislocated, and the dislocation is to the inside parts, then the patient must be laid on his side; and then place the bandages on the root of the groin in that place which is between the head of the groin and the place that is below the collarbone; and then extend the bandage from the top of the collarbone to the highest part of the furcula.
And then another minister strongly presses the arms of him, and warm the thick place of the groin of the patient and extend to the outside parts by vehement extension, for that returns to its place.
And this species is of lighter cure with which this member is reduced than the others.
But if it is excused over you and does not obey the entrance with this species of cure of all, then it is necessary that the two legs of the patient are tied together with a strong, light bandage, on both the ankles and both the knees.
And the length of each of its parts is the quantity of four fingers, and the leg of the patient extended more than the other by the quantity of two fingers.
And then the patient is suspended over the top of the pole, and that he is in the middle; and the length of him from the ground is the quantity of two arms.
And then command a strong young man to pull the head of the groin, and that he is suspended with the patient another young man, and the other young man pulls the groin with strength and pushes, for the joint returns to its place with speed.
But in the proper reduction, when the dislocation is to the outside part, then the patient must lie on his stomach according to what we have recommended in the having of the groin; and be tightened the bandage on the leg of the patient properly and on his feet.
And then two poles are placed, one at his feet, and the other at the head; and then poles are placed adjusted in the middle of the groin, on which damp cloths are enveloped, so that the patient is not damaged because the pole is between his thighs, for that the extension to the inside parts is not pulled.
And then each minister extends his part, and the doctor with his hand engulfs the reduction according to the art.
And when the dislocation is to the front parts, then the leg must be extended slightly, and it is according to this same narration about groin; and the doctor places the palm of his right hand on the groin of the patient, and then pulls that with the other hand, and with that pull he pauses that extended to the inside parts to the part of the knee.
And if the dislocation is to the back parts, then the patient must not be extended to the inside parts, and it is elevated above the ground; he must be placed on a hard cause, as if the dislocation is to the outside parts, according to what we have said of the placing of him on two planks; and it is on his back and the bandages are extended, as we have said, there is no harm.
And it must be administered compression with a board over the place where the joint is.
Therefore, as the reduction is complicated according to what you must — the sign of the reduction of him is not hidden from you, and it is that you extend from the patient two legs, and when you see those engulfs and the patient extends his leg and expands that his excuse, then you know that the member according to what you must is returned — and then you adjust two bandages and pause ointment and extend with bandage so that the width is not harmed in any of the parts; and adhere the patient to rest for three days or for four.
And then untie the bandage and the ointment, and compare one leg with the other.
Now, if you see those joints in alignment, then you know that the dislocation is already fixed, and therefore let the patient go.
And if you see any cause for softening, then you return and plaster that, and stretch that according to your first structure, and leave it for three days.
And then unwrap that, and make that one delay in walking for a few days, until it is comforted.
Chapter .xxxii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the knee.
The knee is dislocated in three ways, which is dislocated to the outside parts, and to the inside parts, and to the parts in front to the parts behind; and to the front parts it is not dislocated.
And the sign of dislocation of it is that you command the patient to apply his leg to the thigh; then you know that the knee is dislocated.
And the restoration of all the ways of it is that you make the patient straight, so that he already extends his leg, if he can above that; adhere your two hands to the face of it, and place his foot between your feet; and then make adhere the knee of it to your palms, and keep those between your fingers on the knee of it with strength, and another minister extends his leg while the knee returns to its place.
And the sign of the return of it is that his leg adheres to the thigh with lightness without labor.
And then plaster that and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and then tie those immediately with a bandage for three days or for four, and then unwrap those.
And do not use the patient for walking for a few days, until it is healed and comforted.
But if the reduction of it to you is excused, then administer strong extension with ligaments of which in the cure of the hamstring preceding narrative.
Chapter .xxxiii.
Of the cure of the dislocation of the ankle.
The ankle some times is dislocated by small movement, and some times is dislocated according to compliment, and the dislocation of it is made either to the inside parts or to the outside parts.
And the sign of the dislocation of it is that you see the ankle inflated proceeding to the part to which it is dislocated.
But the cure of the dislocation of it is of lightness reduction, and is that it be extended with facility with the hands and be aligned while it returns.
But in the cure of it when it is dislocated according to compliment, it is necessary that you make the patient straight, and have one strong and valiant minister of the part behind the two of it in the middle location of it.
And then you with your right hand the foot of the most sovereign part, and with your left hand of the part more below the foot in the location of the ankle.
And then you pull the foot to you with your right hand, and with the left for two times, and then extend with the left; and push the foot of the foot with the right, so that the leg works.
And do this two times according to that we have counted.
And then push the foot of the foot to the leg the third time, and you are at the ankle.
Therefore if it returns in one time or in two according to this manner, and if you see the foot aligned, it is good; and if not, then over it iterate the operation, because that returns.
But if to you is forbidden the reduction of it with that we have recounted, then make the patient lie on his two on the ground, and stretch a padded mat on the ground firm, and that it sits between the thighs of it, and you already have enveloped over it cloth so that it does not scratch the patient.
And then the minister of it holds its thighs, and another minister extends the leg with its hands or with a ligament that lies on the collar of the foot; and then extend that each minister against extension of its part, and the mat be extant between the thighs of the patient retaining that, so that the body of it not be pulled to the parts below because of its extension.
And then the physician aligns the dislocation with its hands, and another minister holds the healthy thigh to the parts below, because the dislocation returns with facility.
And therefore when it returns the dislocation and is declared to you the health of the reduction of it, then pause plaster and extend that with ligaments strongly, and tie the foot with ligaments to the leg.
And be careful and guard yourself of the nerves which are behind over the ankle, so that the ligament over it not be vehement and injure it strongly.
And then leave it for two days or three; and if the ligament is softened, extend it.
And then unwrap it on the third day or on the fourth, and prohibit the patient from movement for forty days. But if it is forced to go before that space, it is not done safely that the dislocation not be over it dissolved and corrupted, and then that it does not receive cure.
And if it happens to it an abscess, then you must administer in the reduction of it that in the location of our narration, in another place of cure and of embrocation, until it is healed.
Chapter .xxxiiii.
Of the cure of dislocation of the toes.
So that the one that is dislocated be straightened with little extension of his work; and that which is not difficult, lift it lightly.
But if the dislocation is in some joints of the foot, then you must make the patient put his foot on a level place of the earth or on a table, and standing thus as if he were going.
And then you stand beside his feet, and place your foot upon that which encroaches from the joints, and then press it with your foot with virtue until it returns, and that you see it already straightened and does not appear in the place eminence.
And then place under the foot of him a table that supports the whole foot, which has two heads, and then strengthen it with a decent and firm structure for three days; and then untie it and make him rest from walking for many days, until it is strengthened and its return is assured.
Chapter .xxxv.
Of the kinds of dislocation that are made with plague or with fracture or with any of them together.
When any of those causes occur, and you are engaged in the cure of it and in the restoration of it, many times it happens that death occurs.
And for this reason you must not presume over the cure of it, but rather the one who is wise in the art, of long usage, merciful and compassionate, tardy, not bold nor presumptuous; and that uses in the beginning of medicines that cause abscesses as little as possible, and leaves the patient to the divine judgment, except to the one whom you hope for salvation from perdition, with the alleviation of the illness, and in which appears some hope. And therefore strive as soon as possible to make the reduction of it at the beginning of the cause, before it becomes an abscess.
And therefore if the limb returns as we want, then administer the regimen which causes abscesses and cures the plague with what is convenient for it of the dried herbs.
And if the dislocation is with a fracture and it happens in the bones separated, then you pierce the stem of them, and do in that what we have said in the simple illnesses of that which is preceded in the places of those.
And guard and avoid according to your virtue that of the instrument in the ways of fear according to what has preceded you my preaching; for this is better to you, you owe your Creator, and more permanent to your glory, and more greetings to your true body in your time. Thus ends the words of Albucasim perfectly of which may God be the benefit. Amen.
